## [2026-07-09] update | NOTE: config/models.json switched qwen 35B → gemma-4-26b-a4b-qat (EXTERNAL change, not this agent)
The Stop hook flagged `config/models.json` as modified. The diff shows `text_model` + `vision_model` switched from `qwen/qwen3.6-35b-a3b` → **`google/gemma-4-26b-a4b-qat`** (plus a cosmetic em-dash → `—` re-serialization, the signature of a JSON writer — i.e. the dashboard model-picker or a manual edit re-saved the file). **This was NOT edited by this session's work** — I only load/unloaded models via `lms` for benchmarking and never touched `config/models.json`. Recording it because it is a real behavior change and it invalidates transfer of this session's numbers: the **50 tok/s baseline, the 8× spec-decode result, and all run timings were measured on qwen 35B** and do NOT carry over to gemma-4-26b-a4b-qat (different arch, 4B active vs 3B, ~15.6 GB vs ~22 GB — likely fits the pool with more headroom, possibly faster, unmeasured). Left the file AS-SET (owner's runtime choice — not reverting, not committing on their behalf); the [[hot]] state table still lists qwen and will be updated only once the owner confirms the switch is intentional. No wiki content changed by me for this — it is an external runtime-config change, surfaced to the owner. Pages: [[hot]] (note only).

## [2026-07-09] update | Companion punchline-only shorts feature (CLIP_COMPANION_SHORTS, default off)
Built the owner's clip-review idea: for a long clip with a strong late payoff, ALSO emit a short punchline-only version ("post the full clip AND a small ending clip for quick sharing"; motivating example = the 'Yo!' Freestyle). `stage7.py:_maybe_companion_short` runs right after the full clip renders + before cold-open. **Design choice that made it clean:** the short is a straight sub-cut of the FINISHED clip (ffmpeg `-ss/-t` + NVENC), NOT a re-render — so captions (burned-in) + blur-fill + colors + 9:16 are inherited and stay ALIGNED for free (a re-render would misalign because `clip_<T>.srt` is 0-based per-clip from `clip_audio_<T>.wav`). Window = payoff-centered `[T−5, T+10]` rendered-time (`payoff_r=(T−clip_start)/speed`), start snapped to a word boundary via the SRT. Gates: flag on; full ≥30 s (owner's example is 36 s, so the ">45" starting suggestion was too high); short ≥6 s AND <75% of full; exempt `storytime,emotional` (payoff-only loses their buildup) but NOT rap/freestyle (the owner's use case, opposite of P-TIGHT). ADDITIVE + failure-soft; env-tunable (`CLIP_COMPANION_LEAD_S/_TAIL_S/_MIN_FULL_S/_MIN_S/_EXEMPT`). Wired into both the legacy and profile render paths. **Verified live** on the real 36 s 'Yo!' clip → 11 s ending short (captions inherited); storytime + <30 s correctly skip; flag-off = no-op. Pages: [[concepts/clip-rendering]]; files: `scripts/pipeline/stages/stage7.py`.

The existing A/B **1.15× clears 1.1×** → speed gate PASSES. Remaining gate = owner reviews the parallel run's 10 rendered clips in `clips/` (6 differ from serial: 2× 'Freestyle' hype, 'Principal Addresses…', 'Waiting for the Principal', 'Caught Lying About His Sister', 'Samurai Slicer Diss'). **Stays flag-gated (default-off) until the owner OKs; then one-commit flip to default-on.** Value concentrated on long VODs (Lacy Stage-4 ~3h → ~30 min saved). ## [2026-07-09] update | Moment-parallel REJECTED by its gate (1.15×, 4/10) → reverted; LLM floor now FULLY closed
The A/B verdict came back REJECT on BOTH pre-agreed gates (`moment_ab_20260709_141429.json`): **Stage-4 speedup 1.15×** (serial 1107 s → workers=2 959 s; gate ≥1.4×) and **clip overlap 4/10 ±20 s** (gate ≥5/10). Root cause consistent with every prior concurrency measurement on this rig: LM Studio co-batches the concurrent requests into shared forward passes, and the cross-vendor Vulkan split's per-pass coordination cost barely amortizes across a batch — the same floor that made spec-decode 8× SLOWER and card-parallel ~4%. The textbook 2-stage-pipeline 2× never materializes because the bottleneck is per-pass sync, not idle compute. **Action per the no-zombie rubric: `stage4_moments.py` reverted to the pre-parallel state same day** (thinking wiring kept; serial arm had validated the extraction live — 1107 s ≈ the 1156 s historical median, exit 0, 10 clips). Gate driver `moment_parallel_ab.py` + verdict JSON kept as forensics. **Consequence: findings §7 is now UNCONDITIONAL — all software levers on Stage-4 LLM time are measured and dead (parallelism 1.15×, spec-decode 0.12×, prefix ~1 min, cards ~4%); the only remaining levers are hardware (single big card) or a model-tier change.** New §7b records the A/B. Pages: [[concepts/pipeline-speed-findings-2026-07]] §7b, [[concepts/plan-serving-stack-2026-07]] §0, [[hot]]; files: `scripts/lib/stages/stage4_moments.py` (reverted).

## [2026-07-09] update | Moment-parallel WIRED (owner approved variance gate over byte-identity); A/B gate launched
Owner asked why the pipeline never sends concurrent requests, what the 7/10-vs-5/10 yardstick means, challenged byte-identity as a quality gate ("non-byte-identical should be fine — byte identity doesn't correlate with clip quality"), and approved wiring moment-parallelism + the gated A/B. **Answers filed**: the pipeline was serial by DESIGN-ERA policy (byte-hash validation), not a technical blocker — the serving side has had PARALLEL=4 slots all along; the yardstick = two plain serial temp-0.3 runs of the same VOD only share 5/10 clips (sampling noise), while concurrency-vs-serial shared 7/10 → concurrency changes the clip set LESS than a re-run already does; byte-identity remains the right gate only for cache/lifecycle levers (a non-identical cache hit is a bug), never for LLM generation — the owner's framing matches the gate-class doctrine. **Wired (Speed #5 cut-over 2)**: `CLIP_PASSB_MOMENT_WORKERS` (default 1=off) in `stage4_moments.py` — mechanical extraction of the 165-line post-call block into `_process_moment_response()` (serial path now calls it, behavior-identical; scripted refactor, exact-marker based); parallel mode: `_eager_card_summary()` appends chunk N's prior-context summary at SUBMIT time from the PRECOMPUTED card (two-phase Phase-A semantics; forces `_card_workers=4` on; documented divergence: summary present even if N's call fails — 0.49% rate, 2-chunk window, retry queue recovers) + ≤N in-flight futures with 1-chunk-lag drain (grounding/speaker post-processing on the main thread overlaps in-flight calls) + post-loop drain (outage-break safe). **Gate launched** (`scripts/research/moment_parallel_ab.py`, bg): 2xRaKai serial arm (also live-validates the refactor) vs workers=2 arm; PROMOTE iff Stage-4 wall ≥1.4× AND scored-clip overlap ≥5/10 ±20 s; verdict JSON to diagnostics. Promote-or-delete on result per the no-zombie rubric. Pages: [[concepts/plan-serving-stack-2026-07]] §0, [[hot]]; files: `scripts/lib/stages/stage4_moments.py`, `scripts/research/moment_parallel_ab.py`.

## [2026-07-09] update | Double-launch GUARDED (cross-process pid marker); gemma re-tested; Stage-4 timeline corrected
Owner Qs answered + the double-launch fixed. **(1) gemma re-test** (owner manually toggled thinking OFF): 0 reasoning_tokens in ALL rows including `enable_thinking=True` → gemma obeys the MODEL/template-level toggle, IGNORES the per-request kwarg in both directions. Since qwen (same LM Studio, same request path) honors the kwarg, LM Studio IS forwarding it — so it's **gemma's chat template not wiring the per-request `enable_thinking`**, not an LM Studio bug. The owner's manual toggle-off is the correct fix; gemma-thinking-off works (0 reasoning, correct answer). **(2) Timing**: VOD 1 Lacy = **5 h 52 m (21155 s)** to complete 20 clips — but Lacy is a 6.8 h VOD (~61 Stage-4 chunks) that takes ~5.5 h even healthy (realtime 0.82); the gemma/contention overhead added ~20 min. **(3) Stage-4 "failure" corrected**: not a clean 100% fail — gemma-thinking-ON reasoned ~7997 tok/moment-call → ~6 min/chunk (many empty-content, some 0-1 moments). Lacy limped through (Stage 4 ~4.5 h); Jynxzi was still grinding chunk ~16 after 1.5 h when the PC crashed → never finished. **(4) Double-launch FIXED**: `is_pipeline_running()` now also checks the on-disk `pipeline.pid` marker (`_marker_pid()`/`_pid_alive()`, `pipeline.done`-aware) → cross-process, so the owner's start→stop→restart-dashboard→play no longer double-launches (2nd play returns 409); `api_stop`→`stop_running_pipeline()` kills the marker pid (`taskkill /F /T`) even without an in-memory handle. Logic unit-tested (live→running, done→finished, dead→not). BUG 67 concurrency-guard TODO closed. Validated: qwen live=0→pass, mock 200→abort, mock 0→pass. **CORRECTION to the same-day finding:** the "gemma ignores ALL controls / permanent reasoning" result was measured while gemma was loaded with thinking ON (owner's UI template edit). Fresh reload (default template) → gemma reasons **0** and answers correctly → gemma-thinking-OFF is usable; the request kwarg is honored by qwen, ignored by gemma, but the MODEL/template level controls it (the `operation.enableThinking` config field does NOT — confirmed). BUG 67 amended with the refinement + shipped fix. All files syntax+import+env-chain verified. ## [2026-07-09] query | Thinking-control verification: pipeline uses the RIGHT commands; qwen obeys, gemma ignores all (proven)
Owner asked to verify the pipeline's think/no-think commands + wants a reliable programmatic + dashboard thinking toggle. **Reviewed:** every LLM caller (`lmstudio.py`, `stage3_segments.py`, `stage4_moments.py:call_llm`, `stage4_rubric.py`, `callbacks.py`, `grounding.py`, `vlm_judge.py`) already sends `chat_template_kwargs:{enable_thinking:False}` + prefixes `/no_think` + has a `reasoning_content` fallback + budgets tokens — the correct, complete standard stack. **Live A/B proof** (`test_thinking_control.py`, same prompt, kwarg False/True × /no_think on/off): **qwen3.6-35b-a3b = 0 reasoning_tokens every case** (control works); **gemma-4-26b-a4b-qat = ~200 every case, identical regardless of kwarg or /no_think** → ignores ALL request-level control (per-model `enableThinking:false` also failed). Web-confirmed ([lmstudio docs/blogs]): request `chat_template_kwargs` overrides server defaults FOR MODELS WHOSE TEMPLATE READS IT; gemma's only lever is a chat-TEMPLATE edit (`{%- set enable_thinking = false %}`), a per-model UI op. Side-finding: qwen `enable_thinking=True` per-request also gave 0 → the "thinking ON" direction is gated by model-level config, not the request kwarg. Conclusion: thinking control is **model-dependent**; a dashboard toggle can reliably drive the request-level control for COMPLIANT models (qwen) but cannot force gemma off. Documented in BUG 67 (proof numbers). Pages: [[concepts/bugs-and-fixes#BUG 67]], [[hot]].

Answers the Lever-2 question: gemma-4-26b is a NO-GO drop-in (fails on OUTPUT FORMAT, not speed). (B) TWO identical `run_pipeline.py --vods … --force` were running under different interpreters (`.venv` + `Program Files\Python312`) = **two dashboard instances**; `pipeline_lock` is per-process so neither guarded the other → shared work dir (marker clobber = phantom "stuck", no clean done → no `run_metrics` row) + shared LM Studio (contention amplifying A). **Fixes/cleanup:** `git checkout config/models.json`→qwen (known-good), removed stale markers (pid/stage), cleaned leftover `clipper_prefetch_*.wav`. **Verified NO git data loss** (all Wave-2 commits present, BUG 66 intact). ## [2026-07-09] query | Dashboard inherits Wave-2 defaults (verified) + the 8× spec-decode mechanism documented
Owner asked (a) whether the non-quality speed wins run automatically via the dashboard UI and (b) WHY speculative decoding is 8× slower. **(a) Verified by tracing the launch path:** the dashboard's bare-metal path runs `python scripts/run_pipeline.py` (`dashboard/_state.py:38`) via `spawn_pipeline()` with `pipeline_env()` = `os.environ.copy()` + model/caption/originality vars ONLY — grep-confirmed it sets none of `CLIP_SEGMENT_CACHE`/`CLIP_BATCH_PREFETCH`/`CLIP_STAGE2_ALWAYS_UNLOAD`, so the code-level defaults win → C3/C4/C1 + Wave-1 all run automatically. C1 only fires on batch modes (dashboard "process all"=`--all`, multi-select=`--vods a,b` — both single-process batch loops); single-VOD = harmless no-op. **Landmine:** the Docker path (`CLIP_USE_DOCKER=1`) runs the legacy bash `clip-pipeline.sh`, NOT run_pipeline.py → gets NONE of Wave 1/2. **(b) 8× mechanism (economics inversion):** spec decoding needs `draft_cost ≪ target_cost`; on the coordination/bandwidth-bound cross-vendor Vulkan split per-pass time is set by the fixed cross-GPU sync (not matmul size — the §7 floor), so a 2B pass ≈ a 35B pass → `draft_cost ≈ target_cost`, assumption violated → K draft + verify + reject-redo passes multiply work ~8× (20ms/tok → 167ms/tok). Catch-22: the fix (cheap draft on a single card) needs the 35B to fit one card — the very thing the split exists to avoid. Filed: plan §0a (dashboard reachability + Docker warning), findings §9b (mechanism + catch-22), findings Bottom-line (Wave 2), [[entities/dashboard]] note. Pages: [[concepts/plan-serving-stack-2026-07]], [[concepts/pipeline-speed-findings-2026-07]], [[entities/dashboard]], [[hot]].

## [2026-07-09] update | C1 A/B PASSED → promoted DEFAULT-ON (contention +0.1%); C2b deleted
C1 contention micro-benchmark result: NVENC render median **16.9 s alone vs 16.9 s during a concurrent whisper job at 88% GPU util = +0.1% slowdown** (35B evicted, matching the real overlap condition). The NVENC encoder ASIC and whisper's CUDA cores are different silicon → they don't contend. So C1's overlap of the next VOD's Stage 2 with the current VOD's ~5.6 min render window is essentially free → **saves ~5.6 min per VOD transition in a batch, byte-safe** (audio-events already proven byte-identical). **C1 promoted to DEFAULT-ON** in `run_pipeline.py` (`CLIP_BATCH_PREFETCH` default 1; kill switch =0; no-op on single-VOD runs). Chose the micro-bench over a ~2.5 h full 2-VOD×2-config batch because C1 is byte-safe so contention was the only failure mode, and the micro-bench measures it decisively in ~6 min vs one noisy datapoint from a 2.5 h run. Wave 2 final scorecard: **C3 + C4 + C1 default-on**; C2b deleted; S1 RED (8× regression); C6 closed. Pages: [[concepts/plan-serving-stack-2026-07]] §0, [[concepts/pipeline-speed-findings-2026-07]] §9b, [[hot]]; files: `scripts/run_pipeline.py`.

Owner: run the C1 A/B, delete C2b. **C2b removed** from `stage4_moments.py` (the `CLIP_PROMPT_STATIC_FIRST` flag + the static-first prompt branch) — its ~1 min/run payoff didn't justify perturbing the tuned core moment prompt (real clip-quality risk) or a 40-min validation run; deleted rather than left a default-off zombie. The C2a prefix-reuse measurement stays in findings §9b for a future revisit. **C1 A/B:** chose the CONTENTION micro-benchmark over a ~2.5 h full 2-VOD×2-config batch (which would give one noisy datapoint for a ~5 min effect) — C1 is byte-safe, so its only failure mode is GPU contention (whisper prefetch vs NVENC render sharing the 5060 Ti with the 35B evicted). Micro-bench measures render-alone vs render-during-whisper directly. Result recorded next. Pages: [[concepts/plan-serving-stack-2026-07]] §0, [[hot]]; files: `scripts/lib/stages/stage4_moments.py`.

## [2026-07-09] update | S1 speculative decoding RESOLVED = measured 8× REGRESSION (no-go); C1 events byte-identical
Owner enabled LM Studio Settings → **"Use LM Studio Engine protocol"** and the Speculative Decoding toggle appeared — asked to re-test S1 without the UI. With engine protocol ON, `lms load qwen/qwen3.6-35b-a3b -c 16384 --speculative-draft-simple --speculative-draft-model qwen/qwen3.5-2b -y` now **LOADS** (previously rejected on native Vulkan). But the benchmark is decisive against it: **decode 6.0 tok/s with the 2B draft vs 50 baseline — 8× SLOWER**, even prefill regressed (cold ttft 6.5→9-18s). Isolated the cause: engine-protocol-**no-draft** = **51.7 tok/s** (the runtime switch is NEUTRAL; the DRAFT is the regression). Root cause = the §7 floor: the cross-vendor Vulkan split is coordination/bandwidth-bound, so the 2B draft's extra per-step cross-GPU passes cost more than they save — speculative decoding is the wrong lever for THIS hardware (it wins only when the draft is near-free + target-verify is the bottleneck). **S1 → RED (no-go), do not wire the draft into `load_model()` even though it now would work syntactically.** Engine-protocol setting safe to leave on either way; draft qwen3.5-2b kept on disk (1.9 GB) for a future single-card experiment. Also: **C1 live gate — audio-events BYTE-IDENTICAL** through the isolated prefetch path (originals restored); its transcript compare was confounded by a whisperx→faster-whisper symlink-privilege fallback (env non-determinism, not a C1 defect) and the fallback made the prefetch 20.6 min > the ~5.6 min render window → C1 correctness proven but wall-clock benefit UNproven → stays flag-gated pending a 2-fresh-VOD batch A/B. Pages: [[concepts/plan-serving-stack-2026-07]] §0/§3a, [[concepts/pipeline-speed-findings-2026-07]] §9/§9b, [[hot]].

## [2026-07-09] update | #5 caveat REFRAMED by the variance yardstick — concurrency noise < existing sampling noise
Owner asked whether #5's caveat can be mitigated. Measured the missing yardstick from committed data: two SERIAL production-temp (0.3) runs of the SAME rakai VOD (frozen `20260705_010127` vs `_074956`) overlap only **5/10 clips (±20s)** — the pipeline's NORMAL run-to-run sampling variance. Card-parallel-vs-serial at temp 0 measured **7/10**. So **concurrency-induced variance is SMALLER than the sampling variance every production run already has** — the "changes the clip set" caveat is not a new quality risk, it's within existing noise (a different draw from the same distribution, which every re-run produces today). Recorded in [[concepts/pipeline-speed-findings-2026-07]] §3-reframe. Consequence: enabling `CLIP_PASSB_CARD_WORKERS` is defensible with a one-batch owner spot-check; the serial-vs-serial-yardstick A/B is the correct gate for any future moment-parallel work (not byte-hashing). ## [2026-07-09] update | Speed #6 BUILT + VALIDATED (zero-flip on 2 real VODs) but default-off — dominated by #2
Built #6 fully per owner request. `_scan_vectorized` in `audio_events.py` (`AUDIO_EVENTS_VECTOR`, default off): block-HPSS (one per ~600s block) sliced per window for music_dominance (the ~700ms/window dominant + only context-dependent detector); crowd + rhythmic recomputed EXACT per-window (byte-identical → can't flip); near-threshold music hybrid-recomputed exactly; straddle windows fall back. Wired vector>threads>pool>serial + `--vector` CLI. **Validated (CPU-only, no LM Studio):** `vector_equiv.py` harness; synthetic + **2 real VODs (2xRaKai + Tylil, 30-min) → ZERO fire flips**. Finding: block-HPSS music deltas reach **0.146** on real audio → raised the hybrid `band` 0.05→0.15 (must be ≥ max error for a guarantee, not luck; rakai max 0.015). **Benchmark = verdict:** vectorized single-thread ~1.9× over serial (2.1 vs 1.1 win/s) — **SLOWER than the shipped DEFAULT threaded scan #2 (~3.3×)**. So #6 is correct + validated but **dominated by #2**; enabling it would slow the scan. **Stays default-off** — the honest completion: I6.0–I6.3 cleared, and the gate revealed it's not worth enabling (threaded scan already won; #1 skips it on re-runs). ## [2026-07-09] update | Speed #5 card-parallel cut-over shipped + VALIDATED → key negative result
Shipped CUT-OVER 1 (card-parallel arc-card precompute, `CLIP_PASSB_CARD_WORKERS` default off; commit 4d1d547) and ran the temp-0 validation. **The hash gate FAILED and the finding is important:** card-parallel fp `78594f460395861e` ≠ baseline `8e0316624c64089a`, 23/25 chunks differ — but chunk 1 (no prior-context) matches exactly and ALL diffs are prior-context summaries; the only changed variable was card concurrency. **Root cause: concurrent temp-0 LLM generation is not bit-identical to sequential (LM Studio batched-inference reorders FP reductions) → cards differ even at temperature 0.** This is inherent to ANY LLM-call parallelization, not a bug. Consequence: different cards → different summaries → different prompts → **a different selected-clip set (7/10 shared ±20s, 3 swapped).** So the plan's byte-identity premise is falsified — LLM-parallel cut-overs can't be byte-validated, only quality-judged by owner review. Given the owner's hard quality line, recommendation: **keep #5 default-off**; cut-over 2 (moment-parallel) hits the same wall with a bigger blast radius → hold. The genuine byte-identical speed wins already shipped (#1 cache, #2 threaded DSP scan, #7 metrics); Stage-4 LLM parallelism is a real speed/reproducibility tradeoff now surfaced with data. Pages: [[concepts/plan-speed56-execution-2026-07]], [[hot]]; files: `scripts/lib/stages/stage4_moments.py` (card-parallel, default off).

## [2026-07-08] update | Speed #5 engine PROVEN in pure logic + #6 harness done, #6 DSP refactor deferred
Executed [[concepts/plan-speed56-execution-2026-07]] to the maximum verifiable-without-LM-Studio extent.
**#5:** built `scripts/lib/passb_driver.py` (serial + two-phase Pass-B, dependency-injected) + `scripts/research/passb_equiv.py` (mock equivalence proof). **passb_equiv PASS** — two-phase byte-equivalent to serial across 6 sizes × 4 worker counts (prompts, moments, summaries), prior-context window, card-failure fallback, failed-chunk set + retry, happy-path breaker. The proof CAUGHT A REAL BUG in pure logic pre-live: serial only creates a chunk's summary after its MOMENT call succeeds (card is inside the `if response:` block), so a transient moment-call failure shortens later prior-context — my first two-phase (all cards in Phase A) diverged. Fixed with an exact **reconciliation pass** (call_llm success is prompt-independent → final success set stable → one pass rebuilds+re-runs only succeeded chunks whose prior-window held a failed chunk; zero cost on the happy path). Two-phase now byte-exact even under transient failures. Remaining for #5 = the LIVE cut-over (wire stage4's real closures into the driver) + live gates (temp-0 hash baseline, workers=3 check, outage drill, soak) — the engine is done + proven. **#6:** built `scripts/research/vector_equiv.py` fire-flip harness (I6.0 old-vs-old PASS: 0 deltas / 0 flips); did NOT build the block-STFT vectorization — **ROI reassessed and deferred**: #2 (threads now default 4) + #1 (cache) already collapsed the scan cost, leaving only a ~3 min gain on fresh scans for a large quality-surfaced DSP refactor. Pages: [[concepts/plan-speed56-execution-2026-07]], [[hot]]; files: `scripts/lib/passb_driver.py` (new), `scripts/research/passb_equiv.py` (new), `scripts/research/vector_equiv.py` (new).

## [2026-07-08] update | Execution plan filed: Speed #5 + #6 with per-iteration validation gates
Owner asked for a structured implementation plan for #5 (two-phase Pass B) and #6 (vectorized scan) with validation testing during iterations. Filed [[concepts/plan-speed56-execution-2026-07]]. Key design work beyond the prior sketch: **(1) validation-design correction** — the earlier "compare prompt hashes workers=1 vs 3" test is CONFOUNDED (cards go through `call_llm` at hardcoded temp 0.3 → summaries stochastic run-to-run even on correct code); replaced with a two-level proof: extract the Pass-B driver into importable `passb_driver.py` with INJECTED call_llm/card fns → `passb_equiv.py` mock harness asserts serial vs two-phase prompt bytes + assembly IDENTICAL (pure logic, no LM Studio), plus a `CLIP_PASSB_DETERMINISTIC=1` temp-0 live integration check. **(2) #6 fire-equality by construction** — byte-equality impossible (STFT center-padding at window edges); ship gate = zero per-window gate flips, GUARANTEED via a near-threshold hybrid (any window with a dial within ±0.05 of a consumed threshold is recomputed exactly with the old path). Each iteration ends compilable+committed with its gate evidence; stop-rule: a gate failing twice → re-plan, never ratchet tolerances. Pages: [[concepts/plan-speed56-execution-2026-07]] (new), [[concepts/plan-pipeline-speed-2026-07]], [[index]], [[hot]].

## [2026-07-08] update | Speed #2 PROMOTED TO DEFAULT — threaded audio scan now on for every run
Owner: turn on the safe win. `audio_events._resolve_thread_count()` default changed 0→`min(4,cores-2)` (=4 on the i9-13900K, 32 logical), so the audio-events scan now runs 4-thread by default on every pipeline run (no env needed). Added runtime BLAS pinning in `_scan_threads` via **threadpoolctl** (`limits=cores//n_threads`) so `threads × BLAS ≤ cores` — the thread path couldn't use the process pool's OMP=1 env pin (numpy already imported). Re-verified: DEFAULT threaded path is **byte-identical to forced serial** + `_resolve_thread_count()`=4 + 3.6 vs 1.1 win/s (3.3×). The `--audio-workers 1` serial mitigation is now obsolete (threads supersede the spawn-prone process pool; `AUDIO_EVENTS_THREADS=1` forces serial). Combined with #1 (cache), a re-run now skips the scan entirely and a fresh scan is ~3× faster. Pages: [[concepts/plan-pipeline-speed-2026-07]], [[hot]]; files: `scripts/lib/audio_events.py`.

## [2026-07-08] update | Durable label store: freeze training data -> trace pile safe to delete
Owner: make Paths B+C safe to clean up by having them keep their own copy of what training needs. Root issue: labels were POINTERS into `clips/.diagnostics/last_run_*.json` traces (gitignored), so deleting a labeled trace orphaned the label — and the fit needs the labeled moment's features PLUS the run's ~240 negatives PLUS the full set for the gate's recall@N, i.e. the whole trace. Built `scripts/research/label_store.py` + committed `learning/frozen_runs/<run>.json`: `merge_labels` auto-freezes every labeled run's FULL candidate set (features only, no media, ~230 KB/run) + its labels into the store (additive, idempotent, B1-only). `fit_ranker --frozen learning/frozen_runs` trains + gates entirely from the committed store — verified byte-identical verdict to the trace path (REJECT, fitted 0.417/baseline 0.5), so it survives a diagnostics wipe / fresh checkout. `scripts/research/prune_traces.py` safely deletes traces that are unlabeled OR frozen (keeps newest 8; refuses to orphan a labeled-but-unfrozen trace; dry-run default, --apply to delete) — 124/132 traces (~28 MB) prunable now with zero risk. Reference-clip `.cache` stays regenerable (source clips kept) + their Path-C labels freeze durably. ## [2026-07-05] update | P-TIGHT head REBUILT content-adaptive (owner: no fixed length)
Owner: "I want shorter clips for certain classified clips but NOT a fixed length — content is highly variable." The v1 head used a fixed 6 s lead (`payoff − head_lead_s`) — the one fixed-length element. REBUILT `clip_tighten._natural_head_start`: snaps `clip_start` to the natural beginning of the utterance leading into the payoff = the most recent SILENCE GAP in the audio (streamer's pause before the bit), with the speech-level reference taken from the PAYOFF region (robust when the head window is mostly silence — fixed a bug where p75 of a quiet window collapsed and pauses went undetected), then refined to the nearest transcript sentence boundary. Head length is now DERIVED from content; only head_min_lead_s(2)/head_max_lead_s(12) bound it (guardrails, not targets). Tail was already content-adaptive (ends at the last reaction burst). So NOTHING in a tightened clip has a fixed/target length now. Verified on synthetic audio: short-setup→snap@14 (5.5 s head), late-short→snap@25 (4.5 s, was broken pre-fix), monologue→capped, transcript-snap@14.2, flag-off=identity; **variability proof: same payoff@20 + 3 different setups → heads 3.0/11.0/5.0 s**. Env knobs CLIP_TIGHT_HEAD_MIN_LEAD_S/HEAD_MAX_LEAD_S/HEAD_GAP_MIN_S/HEAD_SILENCE_FRAC. Default OFF unchanged. Files: `scripts/lib/clip_tighten.py`. ## [2026-07-04] update | corpus_refresh 2-3x faster: batch mode (models load once) + 16 threads (was 2)
Owner: "future runs faster, use more cores, don't compromise quality." Root causes of the ~5 min/clip pace: (1) per-clip SUBPROCESS isolation reloaded CLAP+whisper+EasyOCR (~1.5-2 min) for EVERY clip; (2) the launch env carried OMP_NUM_THREADS=2 on a 24-core i9. Fixes in `corpus_refresh.py`, zero quality impact (same models/params/detections — thread count changes speed only): **batch mode (default)** — `_batch_decompose` imports clip_forensics once and loops clips in-process so weights stay resident; per-STAGE hang watchdogs (`_with_deadline`) still bound everything; an in-process failure gets ONE isolated-subprocess retry; `--no-batch` restores the old path. **`_configure_threads`** — forces OMP/MKL/OPENBLAS to min(16, cores) before numpy/torch import (override `CLIP_REFRESH_THREADS`); forced not setdefault so a stray OMP=2 in the caller's shell can't throttle it. Verified: 16 threads configured, batch plumbing decomposed a clip all-stages-ok in 36 s (cached audio scans, fresh OCR). Expected fresh-clip pace ~1.5-2.5 min vs ~5. ## [2026-07-04] update | Owner SFX critique -> adaptive gain + onset-snap timing + corpus_refresh one-command
Owner reviewed the p4cal clips: "SFX kind of quiet compared to the clip because the clips are loud... [quiet-mic clip] more noticeable but came in a little too early... good clips but the sfx isn't that noticeable." Two root causes fixed. **(1) Loudness-adaptive SFX gain** — `gain_db` was absolute (SFX-file-relative) with a 1.5x linear ceiling, blind to program level: a 0 dB boom is buried under loud rap audio, pops on a quiet mic. New `sfx_inject.measure_program_db` (ffmpeg volumedetect on the clip segment) + `adaptive_gain_db` = clamp(program_mean − ref, 0, +9 dB), boost-ONLY (quiet clips unchanged — owner said those are fine), ceiling raised to 4.0x; wired through `profile_render` into both `build_sfx_layer` calls, logged as `sfx-adapt:` + `sfx_adapt_db` in the effects manifest. Env: `CLIP_SFX_ADAPTIVE=0` kill, `CLIP_SFX_REF_DB` (-20), `CLIP_SFX_ADAPT_MAX_DB` (9). Probed the owner's actual clips: Rap Battle −14.9 dB → +5.1, Freestyle −15.7 → +4.3, Shakespeare (quiet mic) −24.9 → +0.0 — **the probe ranks the clips exactly as the owner's ears did**. **(2) Payoff onset-snap** — the anchor sat on the DETECTION timestamp, which lands a beat early. New `sfx_cues._refine_payoff`: snap to the strongest RMS transient rise within [payoff−0.1, payoff+1.2 s] of audio.wav, fallback payoff+0.35 s; riser keeps its 1 s lead from the REFINED payoff. Config: `payoff_delay_s`/`snap_to_onset`/`onset_snap_window_s` in sfx_cues.json. Verified on synthetic audio: detection@7.00 → snapped@7.80 = the planted hit; fallback 7.35. **(3) effects-log stable run stamp** — the "1/10 manifest coverage" was a GROUPING artifact: `run` was strftime-at-log-time so each clip got its own id; now `CLIP_RUN_STAMP` set once per run by run_pipeline (coverage was actually fine). **(4) `corpus_refresh.py`** — the answer to "how often do I run the training": ONE incremental command (decompose new clips w/ `--trim-end 3.5` TikTok-outro cut by default → seed draft notes → re-distill caption_style + transcript_value + corpus_eval). Honest framing recorded: corpus tools = batch distillation, not continuous learning; the trained component is the Phase-4 ranker (needs labels). 32 new clips queued (background, bounded 2h). Files: `scripts/lib/{sfx_cues,sfx_inject,profile_render,effects_log}.py`, `scripts/run_pipeline.py`, `scripts/research/corpus_refresh.py` (new), `config/sfx_cues.json`. ## [2026-07-04] update | ROOT-CAUSE BUG: _bool_env only accepted "true" — silently disabled SFX-anchor + cold-open
Chased the "SFX feel generic" finding to its root: `sfx_cues.build` WORKS (returns boom/riser cues with proper per-kind gains for every category). The bug was `run_pipeline._bool_env` = `os.environ.get(...).lower() == "true"` — it accepted ONLY the literal "true", so the harness's `CLIP_SFX_ANCHOR=1` and `CLIP_COLD_OPEN=1` (numeric) read as **False** → run_pipeline forwarded `CLIP_SFX_ANCHOR=false`/`CLIP_COLD_OPEN=false` to Stage 7 → the acoustic SFX anchor + cold-open teaser NEVER RAN (zero `sfx-anchor:` log lines; clips used profile-synthesized zoom-tied 0dB SFX). This silently disabled 2 of the validation profile's features and affects ALL 13 `_bool_env` flags for anyone using "1"/"yes"/"on". **Fixed** `_bool_env` to accept the standard truthy set ("true","1","yes","on"); verified 9 cases. **Correction:** both prior "validation" runs had SFX-anchor + cold-open OFF — those 🟡s are NOT cleared; a re-run with the fix is needed to actually validate them (flash-cuts + render + detection-fixes WERE genuinely exercised and remain valid). Files: `scripts/run_pipeline.py`. Pages: [[concepts/plan-pipeline-upgrade-2026-07]], [[concepts/handoff-2026-07-03]], [[hot]].

## [2026-07-04] update | Anomaly lane VALIDATED on a real run + watchdog heisenbug fixed (apply_async)
The stall-proofed retry (`anom2`, CLIP_ANOMALY_LANE=1) COMPLETED cleanly (exit 0, all 8 stages) with the transcript reused (~10min saved) — and **the Phase-1 anomaly lane fired end-to-end: `[ANOMALY] lane proposed 4 src=ANOMALY moment(s) from 218 crowd-reaction windows`**. The keystone works on real data. **Stall-proofing held** — the parallel scan hit a heisenbug (`'generator' object has no attribute 'next'` — IMapIterator.next(timeout) works in isolation in BOTH pythons but errored at runtime after 260s) and the outer handler caught it → fell back to serial (1253s) → no hang. **Fixed** by switching the watchdog from `pool.imap().next(timeout)` to `pool.apply_async()` + `AsyncResult.get(timeout)` (rock-solid documented timeout API); venv-verified a 30s-hung worker aborts in 2.1s. So parallel is now both fast AND stall-proof. Files: `scripts/lib/audio_events.py`. Pages: [[concepts/handoff-2026-07-03]], [[hot]].

## [2026-07-04] update | Stall-proofed the audio scan (all 3 speed options + watchdog) — pipeline can no longer hang
Implemented all three speed-recovery options + a hard stall guarantee (owner: "implement all 3 fixes and ensure the program does not stall"). **Option 3 / the guarantee — watchdog + auto-fallback (the real fix):** `audio_events._scan_parallel` replaced the un-timed `for r in pool.imap(...)` (which blocks FOREVER on a wedged worker — the 58-min hang) with a manual `it.next(timeout=AUDIO_EVENTS_RESULT_TIMEOUT)` loop (default 90s); on TimeoutError it terminates the pool and returns ok=False → the caller runs the existing serial path (IDENTICAL output). Verified: a Pool with a 30s-sleeping worker aborts in 2.1s under a 2s timeout. **Option 2:** harness validation profile default `AUDIO_EVENTS_WORKERS=4` (balanced; watchdog covers any count) + `--audio-workers` override. **Option 1:** new `CLIP_REUSE_TRANSCRIPT` flag in `stage2.py` reuses a cached transcript EVEN under --force (deterministic; skips ~10 min re-transcribe) — harness defaults it on + `--no-reuse-transcript` override; added `import os` to stage2. **Result: no-stall guaranteed at TWO layers** (pipeline watchdog ≤90s → serial; harness `wait --stall` ≤10min for any stage) with ZERO quality change (worker count / serial-vs-parallel is a speed knob, same per-window HPSS math). Retry recipe simplified (all knobs are defaults now). Files: `scripts/lib/audio_events.py`, `scripts/pipeline/stages/stage2.py`, `scripts/research/phase_runner.py`. Pages: [[concepts/handoff-2026-07-03]], [[hot]].

## [2026-07-04] update | IMPLEMENTED the serial-scan default + verified stall detection (harness hardening)
Implemented (not just documented) the two fixes from the hang incident. (1) **Serial audio scan is now the harness DEFAULT** — `_VALIDATION_ENV` sets `AUDIO_EVENTS_WORKERS=1` so every validation-profile run is hang-proof; `--audio-workers N` overrides for speed-at-risk. Serial is ~5-6x slower for that ONE Stage-2 step (~13min vs ~2.5min) but produces IDENTICAL output (same per-window HPSS — a reliability knob, NOT quality). (2) **Stall detection verified** — synthetic test (live pid + frozen log, stall=3s) returned reason=stall in 4.3s; `wait` can no longer sit through a 58-min hang. Handoff harness recipe updated to use `wait --stall`. Retry speedup: the hung run already CACHED the transcript, so a no-`--force` retry skips re-transcription (~10min), roughly netting out the serial slowdown. Files: `scripts/research/phase_runner.py`. Pages: [[concepts/handoff-2026-07-03]], [[hot]].

## [2026-07-04] update | INCIDENT: anomaly validation run hung on Stage-2 audio scan (killed) + harness stall-detection added
The flag-ON anomaly-lane validation run (`anom_rakai`) **HUNG for ~58 min** on Stage 2's **parallel audio_events scan** (8-worker multiprocessing + shared memory on Windows) — log frozen at +623.9s ("parallel scan: 8 workers, 1162 windows") with the pid alive but workers blocked (only ~190s CPU used in 58 min wall). The SAME scan completed in 149s on the 0.1 run, so this is an **intermittent Windows multiprocessing/librosa/shared-memory flake — NOT the Phase-1 wiring** (it hangs at Stage 2, before the Stage-4 anomaly lane). Killed the tree cleanly (run_pipeline 17652 → audio-scan subprocess 59380 → 8 workers; verified only unrelated Odysseus python remained). **Two fixes:** (1) **harness stall detection** — `phase_runner wait` now declares `STALL` when `pipeline.log` freezes > `--stall` seconds (default 600) while the pid is alive (the hand-rolled bash watcher only checked done/fatal/dead-pid, which is why the hang went 58 min unnoticed — silence-is-not-success, now enforced). (2) **retry mitigation** — set `AUDIO_EVENTS_WORKERS=1` to force the serial scan (slower but avoids the parallel-hang path). **Status: Phase-1 anomaly-lane wiring remains committed + unit-verified but NOT yet validated on a real run** (the validating run died on an unrelated stage). `phase_state`: anom_rakai=hung_killed. ## [2026-07-03] update | VO deprioritized (owner decision) + A2 overlay-OCR mining mechanics designed
Two owner inputs recorded, wiki-only. **(1) Voiceover decision:** Piper `tts_vo` stays available (dashboard option, default off) but will likely go unused — most TikTok/IG clips get engagement without VO; owner wants to **maximize clipping quality (detection/selection) instead**. [[concepts/master-proposal-2026-07]] workstream C carries the decision callout; the sequence re-ranked (A1 anomaly lane = the headline, C1–C2 optional); memory updated (supersedes the June "transformation outranks detection" framing for the voice lever). **(2) Chat-mining mechanics** (owner asked HOW burned-in chat gets grabbed — fast chat, latency): designed + filed on [[concepts/reference-humor-2026-07]] §A2 mechanics. No second LLM — EasyOCR (already installed) in offline batch; NOT second-by-second (2 h @ 1 fps = 7,200 calls) — two tiers: **chat-velocity without OCR** (frame-diff rate inside the chat ROI, ~2–4 fps = burst detector + reaction-proxy input to A1) then **OCR only bursts/candidate windows** ([T−2, T+20] @ ~1 fps, consecutive-sample diffing keeps only NEW lines, fuzzy dedup ≈ 20–40 calls/candidate). ROI per-channel config (streamer_prompts pattern) + text-density auto-detect. Output `chat_events.json` ({t,velocity} + {t,text}) parallel to audio_events.json → CHAT track in the A1 fused timeline. **Latency modeled**: viewer reactions lag ~5–12 s (broadcast delay + read + typing) → mine forward [T, T+20], attribute bursts backward (B → B−lag), per-channel lag **auto-calibrated by cross-correlating CLAP laughter with chat-velocity**. Caveats: emotes are images (velocity catches, OCR can't read); fast scroll may skip lines (burst n-grams are repeated → high capture). Also fixed a phase-sequence duplication + stale E2 note in the master proposal. Pages: [[concepts/master-proposal-2026-07]], [[concepts/reference-humor-2026-07]], [[hot]].

Option 5's catch-22 follows: Qwen3-Omni-30B-A3B (~18 GB 4-bit) needs the pool the deaf server owns; the hearing servers only fit 7B-class omni (Qwen2.5-Omni-7B ~7 GB) = weaker judge. TMRoPE noted as option 1 done natively. **(2) Filed [[concepts/reference-humor-2026-07]]** — the George Bush clip ("ever heard of George?" + failed push into a bush; the meme reference is never in the VOD). Verdict: "hard to clip" is TRUE for *understanding/presentation*, OVERSTATED for *detection* — split detect/score/present. Key insights: the **audience is the external-knowledge oracle** (laughter + chat literally names the joke — "GEORGE BUSH LMAO" — and chat is already ingested via grounding/Stage 6); the **pun is textually decodable once senses fuse** ("George" spoken + bush seen → both tokens in one context); the **LLM already knows most memes — nobody asks** (a recognition probe is prompt engineering); residual hard case = deadpan+no-reaction (accept). Ranked options: (1) unexplained-reaction proxy lane (shared with the incongruity anomaly-proposer), (2) chat reference mining (solves titling too), (3) `known_format` probe in the 5.5/6 prompts, (4) `config/meme_formats.json` library grown from notes.json/forensics (+ later yt-dlp), (5) omni perception (helps assembly, not knowledge). ## [2026-07-02] query | How clipping works (re-answered) + multimodal-fusion evaluation filed
Owner asked for a how-it-works review (answered from [[overview]] + [[concepts/clipping-pipeline]] — no new page needed) and then: *can the audio + visual senses be CONVERGED for LLM inference, rather than each modality scored separately and merged post-hoc?* (Motivating clips: ReemKnocks bus + GeorgeBush fail — pure cross-modal incongruity; either sense alone isn't funny.) **Evaluation filed as [[concepts/multimodal-fusion-2026-07]]** (no code modified, per owner instruction). Verdicts: "transcription rated then vision rated" = TRUE at proposal time (Stage 4 Pass B prompts are transcript-only; `audio_events` is a numeric Pass-A boost, never prompt content — `stage4_moments.py:101-114,787`), but NUANCED at enrichment — Stage 5.5 judge (`vlm_judge.py:131-142`, frames + transcript window in one prompt) and Stage 6 (frames + context hint) already do genuinely **joint** inference; the structural gap is **sequencing** (joint inference only happens AFTER a transcript-only proposal gate, so conjunction-carried moments are never proposed) plus audio-as-words and stills-not-motion. "Senses only converge via post-segmented scoring" = mostly TRUE in effect. ## [2026-06-21] update | Clip-forensics robustness: TikTok-outro trim + music-bed false-negative fix (from real-clip ground truth)
The owner checked the ReemKnocks output against ground truth and caught two false signals; both fixed + verified. **(1) TikTok download outro polluted analysis:** downloaded TikToks auto-append a ~3 s outro (logo + creator @handle); its whoosh/logo animation + persistent @handle caption were mis-logged as real edits (the `boing`/`whoosh` at 14–16.5 s were the outro, NOT the creator). Added `--trim-start`/`--trim-end` (+ `CLIP_FORENSICS_TRIM_END` env for batches) → `_trim_signals` window-filters every signal to `[start, dur−end]` BEFORE music/censor are built; output now has `duration_s` (analyzed) + `source_duration_s` + `analysis_window`. Verified `--trim-end 4` drops the outro events. **(2) Music bed under speech missed:** probed raw CLAP scores — the suspense bed WAS detected but peaked at **0.267, under the 0.30 floor** (quiet bed under speech → speech dominates the window). Fix: per-label CLAP thresholds in `config/audio_sense_labels.json` (music 0.18, suspense_music 0.20; `_clap_events` now reads per-label `threshold`) + a sustained-run gate in `_music_bed` (≥1.5 s / ≥2 windows) so the lower floor doesn't fabricate beds. Also refined the `added` heuristic: editor bed = under speech AND (abrupt onset OR starts mid-clip >2 s) — the old abrupt-only rule missed faded-in beds. Verified on ReemKnocks: music **6.0–14.0 s, added:true, suspenseful** (matches "music dropped in ~halfway under the talking"); regression-tested (lone blip gated, ambient-from-0 ≠ added, mid-clip = added). Pages: [[concepts/plan-clip-forensics]], [[entities/audio-sense-module]], [[index]], [[hot]]; files: `scripts/research/clip_forensics.py`, `scripts/lib/audio_sense.py`, `config/audio_sense_labels.json`.

## [2026-06-21] update | Clip-forensics Phase 3 + 4b shipped + a hang-proof watchdog (durable fix for runaway tasks)
Two asks: "continue the next phases" and "stop tasks running for hours — catch errors / come back and fix them." **Watchdog (the durable fix):** every heavy stage in `clip_forensics.py` now runs under `_with_deadline` — a daemon worker with a hard wall-clock cap (`_STAGE_DEADLINES`; `--deadline-scale` to tune). On overrun the worker is ABANDONED (dies with the process — the only way to bound C-extension hangs like the old PANNs/librosa stalls, which ignore Python signals/exceptions) and the stage returns its default, so the run finishes with a **partial result**; per-stage `ok|timeout|error|skipped` lands in a `_stages` block + a WARNING line. Total runtime ≤ sum of caps. Unit-verified: a 10 s hang under a 0.5 s cap returns in 0.50 s. (Also confirmed the "running 5 h" tasks were already-dead orphaned harness wrappers — no live python/ffmpeg; TaskStop reported "no task found" for all; cleaned the orphan .output files.) **Phase 3 — `scripts/lib/visual_sense.py`** ([[entities/visual-sense-module]]): `motion_events()` (cv2 frame-diff punches, robust median+MAD threshold, no model, default ON) + `caption_ocr()` (EasyOCR burned-in captions + words/sec, OPT-IN `--ocr`; installed `--no-deps` to protect the rig's pinned `torch 2.9.1+cu130` — verified untouched). **Phase 4b** `_synthesize_style_profile()`: local LLM (LM Studio `qwen/qwen3.6-35b-a3b`, cfg from `config/models.json`) turns the timeline into a structured **style_profile** (pacing/sfx_cues/music/censor/hook/replication_notes) — failure-soft (null if LM down), default ON (`--no-llm`). **Verified on `ReemKnocksClip.MP4`:** motion 9 spikes; OCR 36 frames / 232 words / **13.08 wps** with real text ("boy has to be stopped TikTok @reemknocks"); LLM profile coherent + grounded in 122 s. Phase 4a (audfprint exact-SFX) stays stubbed (needs a seeded SFX library). Plan now **status: shipped**. Pages: [[entities/visual-sense-module]] (new), [[concepts/plan-clip-forensics]] (Phase 3/4b/watchdog callout + status), [[index]], [[hot]]; files: `scripts/research/clip_forensics.py`, `scripts/lib/visual_sense.py`, `requirements-forensics.txt`.

## [2026-06-12] ingest | Hook-engineering research (deep-research, full verify) — cold-open teaser rules + hook-text templates
Ran `deep-research` on research prompt #3 of [[concepts/plan-unoriginality-audio-layer]] (opening-second retention patterns for 60–180 s storytime/informative clips: cold-open teaser, text-hook phrasing, caption density, retention metrics). **Verified cleanly:** 20 sources → 82 claims → 25 verified → **9 confirmed / 16 refuted** → 6 findings. **Filed [[concepts/hook-engineering-2026-06]].** Survivors: hook in first 6 s / proposition in first 3 s + text density 5–10 words/sec (TikTok-ads primary, 3-0); cold-open payoff-teaser is retention-positive **with the critical refinement TEASE≠SPOIL** (preview the climax to open a curiosity loop, keep the resolution for the end — over-resolving backfires); a category-keyed hook-text template library (storytime/informative/hot-take/authority/funny); and "early swipe-away within 1–2 s = weak hook" as the one surviving metric (YouTube Studio "Viewed vs Swiped Away"). **Headline caveat: adversarial review killed (0-3) nearly every numeric threshold** (65/70% 3-s retention, +20% payoff, cut-every-4-s, 1.5-s algorithm decision) as un-sourced folklore — the clipper must derive retention targets from the user's own analytics, not these blogs. No evidence-backed teaser *length* exists (the ~1–2 s flash is a heuristic to A/B-test). Cross-linked to [[concepts/plan-unoriginality-audio-layer]] (prompt #3 DONE, P2 reorder rules), [[concepts/plan-youtube-informative]], and [[concepts/captions]] (hook card + density). ## [2026-06-07] update | BUG 64 — white-flash transitions painted whole clips white (critical regression, fixed)
Reviewed the first full run with **White-flash transitions on** (`20260607_093740_FirstFullAudio4-20`, `flash=on jump=off`): the run completed and `[transitions] flashes=N` applied to clips, but **every flashed clip came out 100% white** (audio fine; `YAVG≈235` at every timestamp). **Root cause (BUG 64):** the flash used chained `fade=t=out:color=white` + `fade=t=in:color=white`, but FFmpeg's `fade` **holds the colour outside its ramp window** (out stays white after; in shows white before) → the whole timeline is white. My pre-merge test only sampled the flash frame (white) and never a control frame, so it slipped through. **Fix** (`scripts/lib/clip_cuts.py`): new `white_flash_boxes()` builds a TRANSIENT flash with `drawbox … enable='between(t,a,b)'` (rise→peak→fall ~0.16 s); fixed both `_build_filter` (live path) and `white_flash_vf`; selftest now asserts `drawbox`+`enable` and no `fade=`. **Verified with a control frame this time:** before 122 / flash 209 / after 121 — only the flash window is white. **Existing white clips are unrecoverable** (the transition pass `os.replace`d the good render) → re-run to regenerate. Files: `scripts/lib/clip_cuts.py`. Pages: [[concepts/bugs-and-fixes]] (BUG 64), [[concepts/transition-animations]].

## [2026-06-06] update | BUG 63 — fix "Stitch short clips" (never fired) + extensive grouping logs
Traced why the dashboard's **Stitch short clips** / **Stitch arcs** toggles never visibly worked. Root cause (BUG 63): a self-contradictory constant set in `scripts/lib/moment_groups.py` — beat cap 12 s, budget 28+4=32 s, min 3 members → **3×12=36 > 32**, so the 3rd beat always overflowed and stitch silently produced **0 groups on every run** (the 20260607 Lacy run had 4 eligible short funny clips and still made 0). Long-standing; Fix 4 (longer clips) worsened the `dur>cap*2` eligibility filter; and it failed silently (no logs). Arc-stitch separately had simply **never been enabled** in any run. **Fix:** budget invariant (`cap 12→10`, `target 28→36` so `target+4 ≥ min×cap`); decoupled eligibility (`STITCH_ELIGIBLE_MAX_DUR=28`, replacing `dur>cap*2`); **peak-centered beats** (center each beat on the moment's `T`/punchline instead of the first N s = the setup); and **extensive `[GROUPS]` logging** in `build_stitch_groups` + `build_arc_stitch_groups` (per-category eligibility, every skip reason, FORMED groups, arc setup→payoff + skip counts). Unit-verified: the old failing input (4 funny @ 15/20/21/24 s) now forms a 4-beat ~40 s group, beats peak-centered, arc-stitch forms 2 setup→payoff groups. **Relation to the transition work:** distinct — `CLIP_JUMP_CUTS` (clip_cuts.py) compresses dead air *within* a clip; arc-stitch splices a far-earlier setup to the payoff; stitch-short is a montage. Files: `scripts/lib/moment_groups.py`. Pages: [[concepts/bugs-and-fixes]] (BUG 63), [[concepts/originality-stack]].

## [2026-06-06] update | Transition animations — white flashes + jump-cut compression (all phases, flag-gated)
Implemented the full transition-animations plan. **Two effects:** white-flash engagement beats + jump-cut compression (drop dead air/rambling, concat with `xfade=fadewhite` to skip to the payoff). **Key architecture decision:** a single **Stage 7d.5 post-pass over the FINISHED clips** (after 7d render, before 7e stitch) — path-agnostic (covers solo + profile) and **caption-safe** (captions are already burned pixels, so cutting the clip cuts them in sync — no live-timeline SRT remap). **New module `scripts/lib/clip_cuts.py`** (fully unit-tested via `--selftest`): `compute_keep_spans` (snap to pauses, protect tail, cap drop-fraction, drop longest dead spans first), `gaps_to_cuts` (rule: drop silences — works without the LLM), `flash_cadence` (rule: seeded engagement flashes), `apply_transitions`/`process_clip_transitions` (the FFmpeg via `venc.py` NVENC). FFmpeg-verified: 12s clip → 7.70s after a 3-6s drop with the white-fade join; flash frame YAVG=235; cut+flash combined 7.78s. **Model inference:** Stage 6 vision prompt gains a gated request for `cuts`/`flashes` (absolute-timestamped transcript) → stored on `edit_plan`; **byte-identical prompt when flags off** (zero risk). `edit_plan.py` schema += `flashes`/`cuts` (validated/clamped). **Policy/P2:** per-category max-drop (`CATEGORY_MAX_DROP`), tail guard, min-keep, flash cap; rule modes degrade gracefully without the model. **Flags** `CLIP_FLASH_CUTS` (off|on) + `CLIP_JUMP_CUTS` (off|gaps|llm|on), env + **dashboard toggles** (Originality panel) via `config_io`/`_state`/`index.html`/`pipeline-ui.js`. All default OFF + failure-soft. Deferred: dedicated text edit-pass (documented). Needs an end-to-end validation run (`CLIP_JUMP_CUTS=gaps` safest first). Files: `scripts/lib/clip_cuts.py` (new), `scripts/lib/edit_plan.py`, `scripts/lib/stages/stage6_vision.py`, `scripts/pipeline/stages/stage7.py`, `dashboard/{config_io,_state}.py`, `dashboard/templates/index.html`, `dashboard/static/modules/pipeline-ui.js`. Pages: [[concepts/transition-animations]] (new), [[concepts/clip-rendering]], [[entities/dashboard]], [[index]].

## [2026-06-06] update | Dashboard port: env override + auto-fallback (fix WSAEACCES startup crash)
The dashboard stopped starting with `An attempt was made to access a socket in a way forbidden by its access permissions` (Windows `WSAEACCES`). Diagnosed: **not** a code regression and **not** an excluded/reserved port range (checked `netsh int ipv4 show excludedportrange` — 5001 not excluded). A background service, **`GT3 mobile service.exe` (PID 4700)**, had started listening on **port 5001** (dualstack `::`), so Flask's bind to 5001 failed. `app.py` hard-coded `port=5001` with no override, so any squatter blocked startup. **Fix** (`dashboard/app.py`): port is now `DASHBOARD_PORT`/`PORT` env (default 5001) and a new `_resolve_port()` test-binds exactly as Flask does and **rolls forward to the next free port** (5001→5012) if taken, printing `Dashboard ready at http://127.0.0.1:<port>`. Also fixed the startup banner to report the real mode (`native (bare-metal)` / `docker exec` / `inside container`) instead of always "docker exec". Verified with the venv: with GT3 on 5001 the dashboard now reports "5001 is in use — using 5002" and serves on 5002 (no crash). Pages touched: [[entities/dashboard]].

## [2026-06-06] query | Reviewed Lacy run 20260606_235356 — Fix 4 STRONGLY validated; arc-guarantee floor too strict on rich VODs
Reviewed the first run with Fix 4 default-on (Lacy VOD, 30 chunks, 12 clips, exit 0, 46m52s, **zero errors** — torchcodec/M3/MMR all healthy on a new VOD). **Fix 4 VALIDATED**: clip durations now span **16/23/27/34/35/40/40/48/66/78/82/89s** (was clustered ~30s pre-fix), ALL with `lp=1.0` — the tightness signal correctly does NOT penalize dense long clips, so a 78s debate + 66/82/89s long-form clips survived selection at full length. Also holding: Fix 1 (REGEN-still-fails=**0**, clean catchy titles), Item A score spread (0.49-0.75), de-tidy (98 moments/30 chunks), churn 11/12. **Finding — arcs didn't render**: A1 found 5 genuine arcs (irony "scored a penalty", contradiction "best goalkeeper", fulfillment "nando's in LA", exposure "I'll show you later") but NONE reached the final 12 and the Phase-2.5 guarantee did NOT fire — almost certainly the quality floor (`CLIP_ARC_GUARANTEE_MIN_RATIO`=0.6 → arc must score ≥0.6× the weakest winner, whose raw was 1.36 → needs ≥0.82; on a content-rich VOD the abundant strong Pass B `setup_external_contradiction`/`storytelling_arc` moments out-score the dedicated arcs). Consequence: arc-stitch (Fix 3) wouldn't trigger either (it needs an arc IN the selection). Arc-flavored CONTENT is still well-represented (many selected clips are setup_external_contradiction/social_callout). **Recommendation**: to showcase Lacy-style arcs, lower `CLIP_ARC_GUARANTEE_MIN_RATIO` (~0.4-0.5) so the top arc gets a slot, then `CLIP_ARC_STITCH=1` to render it as a setup→payoff stitch. **Stage 7 = 585s** (up from ~290 on rakai) is EXPECTED: ~578s total clip-video (Fix 4 longer clips) + 12 clips; NVENC engaged (filtering is the CPU cost, scales with clip seconds). Fix 3/Fix 2 not exercised (flags off). No code changed. Pages: [[concepts/detection-improvements-plan]], [[concepts/clip-duration]].

## [2026-06-06] update | Fix 1 SHIPPED — segment window size is now a knob (measure-first); detection plan complete
Implemented [[concepts/detection-improvements-plan]] Fix 1 in `scripts/lib/stages/stage3_segments.py`: `CLIP_SEGMENT_CHUNK` (default 600s, unchanged) + `CLIP_SEGMENT_OVERLAP` (default 0, read-context only — recorded segments stay nominal/non-overlapping so the adjacent-merge logic is untouched). `CLIP_SEGMENT_CHUNK=300` halves the window for finer granularity (short off-type pockets get their own label) at ~2× the cheap classification calls. Default left unchanged on purpose — this is the measure-first stance: the knob lets the user A/B 300 vs 600 and compare before committing (detection is type-agnostic, so this mainly sharpens chunk-sizing + Pass A thresholds). Compile clean. **All 4 detection-improvement fixes now shipped** (4 length-neutral duration [default on], 3 stitched setup→payoff [opt-in], 2 embedding keywords [opt-in], 1 segment knob [default unchanged]) — each flag-gated + failure-soft, awaiting a validation run. ## [2026-06-06] update | Fix 2 SHIPPED — embedding-similarity signal for Pass A (opt-in; honest finding: short prototypes are weak)
Implemented [[concepts/detection-improvements-plan]] Fix 2 in `scripts/lib/stages/stage4_moments.py`, flag `CLIP_PASSA_EMBED` (default OFF). `keyword_scan` pre-embeds every 30s window's text + the 8 category prototypes (`_CATEGORY_DESCRIPTIONS`, lifted from the legacy Pass B prompt) in ONE batched `callbacks.embed_segments()` call, then adds a capped (1.0), segment-weighted cosine term per category after the keyword loop. Additive + failure-soft (no sentence-transformers → keywords only). **Empirical test (real all-MiniLM)**: window↔one-line-description cosines run only ~0.15–0.27 — hot_take/reactive classified right, but a clear storytime opener mis-mapped to emotional, and at the planned 0.30 threshold NOTHING fired. So the default threshold was lowered to 0.20 (fires clear matches, skips ambiguous), contribution stays ~0.15 signal. This **confirms the user's "is it too crude" instinct** — short prototypes are only mildly discriminative; the recommended follow-up is richer `config/patterns.json` signature prototypes. Shipped as a tunable, harmless-when-off foundation. Compile clean; embedding stack verified working (sitecustomize fix). Pages: [[concepts/detection-improvements-plan]] (Fix 2 SHIPPED + finding).

## [2026-06-06] update | Fix 4 SHIPPED — length-neutral duration (removes the ~30s skew, content-driven)
Implemented [[concepts/detection-improvements-plan]] Fix 4 in `scripts/lib/stages/stage4_moments.py`, flag `CLIP_LENGTH_NEUTRAL` (default on; `=0` restores legacy). **(a)** `_infer_content_window(ts, segments, max_dur)` replaces the flat `DEFAULT_DURATIONS` for boundary-less moments — anchors on the speech segment nearest the peak, grows across contiguous segments (silence gap ≤1.5s) up to 90/150s, ≥15s, with a max-dur cap centered on the peak for over-long anchor runs. **(b)** `_tightness_multiplier(m, segments)` replaces `length_penalty` at the scoring site (`:2557`) — words/sec over the clip window (`_wps_in`, lifted from baseline_contrast) mapped to `[floor,1.0]` (floor 0.85 emotional/storytime/arc/callback, else 0.7); duration is NOT an input, so a dense 70s monologue ≈ a dense 25s clip (no length penalty) while a padded clip is docked. legacy `length_penalty`+`DEFAULT_DURATIONS` retained behind the flag. Compile clean; unit-tested dense-vs-padded, emotional floor, duration-independence, and the content-window cap (300s seg → 90s). Needs a validation run. ## [2026-06-06] query | Detailed implementation plans for the 4 detection fixes + transcription/vision cross-chunk explainer
Filed [[concepts/detection-improvements-plan]] — concrete, file:line-anchored, phased, flag-gated plans for the 4 fixes (mapped by 4 parallel agents). **Fix 4 (length-neutral duration)**: replace `DEFAULT_DURATIONS` symmetric centering (`stage4_moments.py:2379-2396`) with content-aware boundary inference (reuse `boundary_detect.snap_to_word_boundary`/`detect_silence_gaps`), and replace `length_penalty` (`:2363-2377`, applied `:2557`) with a tightness/dead-air multiplier from `_wps_in` (`baseline_contrast.py:88-101`) + silence-gap fraction — duration not an input; category floor for emotional/storytime. **Fix 3 (stitched setup→payoff)**: new `build_arc_stitch_groups()` in `moment_groups.py` emitting 2-member `kind="stitch"` groups (setup snippet + payoff) reusing `stitch_render.py`; both members key off the payoff `timestamp` and override `start`; gate `CLIP_ARC_STITCH`; callbacks first (have `setup_text`), arcs second (only `setup_time`). **Fix 2 (embedding keywords)**: lift the 8 category descriptions (`stage4_moments.py:1657-1665`) to prototypes, reuse `callbacks.embed_segments()` (all-MiniLM-L6-v2), pre-embed windows once, inject an additive capped cosine term after the keyword loop (`:464`); keep keywords; failure-soft. **Fix 1 (finer segments)**: measure-first (detection is already type-agnostic), then 600→300s overlapping windows in `stage3_segments.py` if warranted. ## [2026-06-06] query | Detection walkthrough filed + 4 design answers (segment granularity, keywords, setup→payoff, duration skew)
Filed a consolidated [[concepts/detection-walkthrough]] (Stage 3 segment detection + Stage 4 moment detection — Pass A/B/A1/M3/C — and how they connect, with the 4 known limitations), then answered 4 design questions as [[concepts/detection-improvements]]. **(1) 10-min segment granularity**: reframed — moment detection is type-agnostic (Pass B assigns per-moment category; A1/M3 work on transcript not labels), so a 2-min debate in a gaming stream still gets its clips; the label only affects chunk-size + Pass A threshold. Fix if needed: finer overlapping segment windows (300s). **(2) keyword crudeness**: don't phase out Pass A (it's the deterministic recall net); augment the literal-keyword term with embedding-similarity to category prototypes (reuse the M3 sentence-transformers stack) — keep keywords + shape/audio/speaker signals. **(3) contiguous setup→payoff**: today A1/M3 emit payoff-centered clips (setup as caption); implement a stitched 2-segment clip (setup snippet + payoff jump-cut) reusing the existing `stitch_render.py` concat machinery — makes arc detection actually pay off + renders the Lacy-penthouse archetype correctly. **(4) 30s skew**: don't invert the bias; make duration length-NEUTRAL — replace the per-category default fallback with content-aware boundary inference, and replace the duration-based `length_penalty` with a tightness/dead-air signal, so length follows content (punchy ~15-25s, monologues ~45-90s) with no forced skew. Suggested order 4→3→2→1. No code changed. Verified `stitch_render.py` already concatenates sub-segments (xfade+hooks+subtitles) so #3 is feasible. Pages: created [[concepts/detection-walkthrough]], [[concepts/detection-improvements]]; [[index]].

## [2026-06-06] query | How clip length is decided + chunk windowing — filed as concepts/clip-duration
User asked why clips cluster at ~30s (hard clamp vs model inference), what the per-chunk window length is, and whether the model can infer relevance across chunks (e.g. 7s from chunk N + 25s from N+1 as one clip). Mapped the full chain via two code-mapping agents and filed [[concepts/clip-duration]]. **Findings**: no hard 30s clamp — Pass B LLM picks start/end (trusted within [15,90], [15,150] for storytime/emotional); ~30s skew is emergent from (a) per-category DEFAULT_DURATIONS fallback for moments without LLM boundaries (funny/hype=30) and (b) a score-side `length_penalty` (≤30s ×1.0 … >75s ×0.65) that makes short clips win Pass C selection. Chunks are per-segment-type: just_chatting/irl 480s/8min (60s overlap), debate 360s (45s), reaction/gaming 300s (30s); consecutive chunks share boundary content via overlap. **Cross-chunk**: the model understands relevance (overlap read-context + last-2-chunk summaries + A1 global pass + M3 callbacks), BUT a single clip can't physically straddle a chunk seam — `parse_llm_moments` clamps each clip to its nominal [chunk_start, chunk_end], so a boundary-straddling moment is truncated to one side; A1/M3 emit payoff-centered ~35-45s clips (setup kept as metadata), not contiguous setup→payoff spans. Levers to add variety (not yet done): soften length_penalty for talky cats, force explicit boundary emission, allow overlap-spanning clips. No code changed. Pages: created [[concepts/clip-duration]]; [[index]].

## [2026-06-06] update | Stage 7 GPU encode — h264_nvenc by default (faster export), libx264 fallback
Implemented GPU-accelerated encoding for Stage 7 (the ~290s editing/export stage; Stage 8 is ~3s, nothing to gain there). Found Stage 7 was already parallel (`STAGE7_WORKERS`=4) but encoding `libx264 -preset slow` (CPU) while the GPU sat **idle** — the model is already unloaded before rendering (`run()` → `common.unload_model`, confirmed in the 20260606_201401 log: `unloaded 'qwen…'` right before "Rendering all clips"), so the full GPU is free. Switched the main `_ffmpeg_render` path to **`h264_nvenc`** in `scripts/pipeline/stages/stage7.py`: new `_VENC_NVENC` profile (`-rc vbr -cq 20` + 18M cap ≈ libx264 crf-20 quality), `_resolve_encoder()` reads `STAGE7_ENCODER`=auto|nvenc|libx264 (default auto → one-shot NVENC test-encode probe, use only if it actually works), and `_encode_with_fallback()` retries each clip with libx264 if its NVENC render fails (session limit/driver) so a flaky session never drops a clip. `_ffmpeg_legacy` (libx264) stays as the final safety net. Verified: stage7.py compiles, no dangling `_VENC` refs, NVENC probe works on the RTX 5060 Ti, and a realistic **blur-fill 9:16 + h264_nvenc** test encode succeeds. NVENC accelerates the *encode* only; per-clip filtering (blur-fill/captions) stays on CPU, so the wall-clock gain depends on the filter/encode split — measure on the next run. Pages: [[concepts/clip-rendering]]. **Stage 8**: no change (≈3s, nothing to optimize).

Re-queue dormant (no failures). No regressions/errors — the session's full fix sweep is confirmed end-to-end. No code changed this turn. ## [2026-06-06] query+update | Pass B false-negative analysis filed + two recall gaps closed
Answered "why does Pass B have more false-negative potential + can it be mitigated" and filed it as new page [[concepts/pass-b-false-negatives]] (7 FN sources × mechanism/mitigation/status, the Pass-A-recall-net architecture, verification commands). Then closed the two implementable residual gaps in `scripts/lib/stages/stage4_moments.py`. **Gap #1 — end-of-pass re-queue**: a failed chunk's LLM call (timeout/HTTP 400/connection-refused/empty-content) used to drop every moment in that ~5-min window (`Chunk N: LLM call failed, skipping`). Now failed chunks are captured in `_failed_chunks` and retried ONCE after the main loop (when LM Studio has usually recovered/drained), gated on `not llm_net_outage()`. Recovered moments get segment-boost + `segment_type` + a light grounding pass (denylist+overlap vs chunk, so a hallucinated `why` can't reach Stage 6) + `requeued=True`; M1/arc-card enrichments skipped (recovery > enrichment). Logs `[PASS B] Re-queue recovered N`. **Gap #2 — de-tidy prompt**: the Pass B prompt now says "List EVERY distinct qualifying moment — do NOT stop at a tidy 2-3 …" to counter the model returning a uniform ~3/chunk on dense chunks. **Gap #3** (keep gate `off`) is already the default. Both compile clean; re-queue unit-tested (transient recovery / outage-skip / hallucinated-why-nulled / segment-boost). **Needs a validation run** to see recovery in action. Pages: created [[concepts/pass-b-false-negatives]]; [[index]].

## [2026-06-06] update | 3B SHIPPED — reactivate reaction/engagement axes when chat is absent
Implemented [[concepts/clip-quality-remediation-2026-06]] Fix 3B. The reaction + engagement Pass C axes were near-inert (median mult ~1.0) on the chatless 6/6 VOD because both are chat-dominant by weight (investigation: parallel agent, verified). Reactivated them **only when chat is absent/insufficient** so chat VODs are byte-for-byte unchanged. **engagement_signals.py**: when `observed<=0`, renormalize the surviving `predicted` term (structural, energy-free stance/monologue from conversation_shape) to full weight via `weights_chat_absent.predicted=1.0` — a firm take scores 0.8 instead of 0.32. **reaction_signals.py**: when the chat term is 0, redistribute the dead 0.40 chat weight to audio+rhythm via `weights_chat_absent {audio:0.92, rhythm:0.08}` — a genuine crowd-pop earns ~+8% vs ~+5%, while quiet moments stay ~1.00x (no energy inflation) and the 1.10 multiplier_ceil + 1.35 global clamp remain the energy-bias guards (crowd_response is a gated laughter/cheer detector, not raw loudness). Both gated behind new `weights_chat_absent` config keys in `config/selection_axes.json`. Compile clean; unit-tested chat-absent lift, chat-present unchanged, ceiling capped. **Needs a validation run** on a chatless VOD to confirm improved selection without over-rewarding energy. Pages: [[concepts/clip-quality-remediation-2026-06]] (3B SHIPPED).

## [2026-06-06] update | Fix 5 SHIPPED — A1 arcs can now win selection (cross_validated strip bug + bounded guarantee)
Implemented [[concepts/clip-quality-remediation-2026-06]] Fix 5 / [[concepts/arc-aware-extraction]] Phase 3 in `scripts/lib/stages/stage4_moments.py`. Investigation (parallel agent, claims verified against code) found the "arcs never win" symptom was a **bug**, not just tuning: arcs are created `cross_validated=True` (high-signal skeleton evidence) but the Pass C dedup loop did `if not merged: m["cross_validated"] = False` (`:2240`) — a hard reset that stripped the flag (and its ×1.20 boost) from every standalone arc, contradicting the "first-class … cross_validated=True" intent. **Fix A**: `:2240` → `m.setdefault("cross_validated", False)` (arcs/callbacks keep creation-time True; keyword/LLM still default False). **Fix D**: new Phase 2.5 after bucket selection — if no arc won a slot, swap the single highest-`final_score` arc in for the weakest selected clip; bounded to ONE swap, spacing-safe, quality-floored (`CLIP_ARC_GUARANTEE_MIN_RATIO`=0.6 so a weak arc can't evict a much stronger clip; `CLIP_ARC_GUARANTEE=0` disables). Honors "a missed clip costs more than a false positive" without flooding. Filed as [[concepts/bugs-and-fixes#BUG 61]]. Compile clean; unit-tested 5 cases (swap-in / quality-floor reject / already-present no-op / spacing-skip / disabled). **Needs a validation run** + `judge_tournament` to confirm guaranteed arcs win pairwise (original Phase-3 decision rule). ## [2026-06-06] update | torchcodec ACTUALLY fixed + Pass B gate label correction (multi/sample were swapped)
Two things this turn, both prompted by the user. **(1) torchcodec — re-examined and genuinely fixed** (supersedes the prior "infeasible" Fix 4): `torchcodec==0.7.0` has a cp312 wheel with NO torch pin and imports fine against torch 2.8; the only blocker was missing FFmpeg *shared* libs. The host has a complete FFmpeg 7.0 shared set in `C:\Program Files\AMD\CNext\CNext` (AMD GPU driver — stable on this AMD-GPU box). Installed torchcodec (pinned in `requirements-speech.txt`) and added `_enable_torchcodec_ffmpeg()` to `speech.py`: at import it finds a complete FFmpeg shared dir (`CLIP_FFMPEG_SHARED_DIR` override → AMD CNext → DaVinci → Blender), `os.add_dll_directory()`s it (handle kept alive), then eagerly imports torchcodec so pyannote reuses it; graceful fallback to soundfile + warning-suppress if unavailable. Verified end-to-end: `AudioDecoder` decoded a real 16 kHz WAV (shape (1,8000)); `import speech` auto-enables via the AMD libs. **(2) Pass B gate labels were BACKWARDS** — found while reiterating the gate for the user. The dashboard dropdown and the wiki table both had `multi` at ~10%/very-low-FN and `sample` at ~22%/low-FN. That's inverted: `sample` = `multi`'s identical 6-signal `_alive` check PLUS a 1-in-N forced LLM pass-through on dead chunks (`stage4_moments.py:1413-1436`), so `sample` skips a strict SUBSET of what `multi` skips → `sample` is SLOWER (less lift) and STRICTLY SAFER (lower FN) than `multi`. Correct ordering by both axes: off < sample < multi < strict. Fixed `dashboard/templates/index.html` (reordered to a monotonic gradient + swapped the two labels + clearer tooltip) and the [[concepts/pipeline-optimizations-2026-06]] table (+ a correction callout). Only the ordering is rigorous; the percentages remain rough estimates. ## [2026-06-06] update | Fix 4 SHIPPED — silence benign torchcodec warning (install infeasible)
Implemented [[concepts/clip-quality-remediation-2026-06]] Fix 4 in `scripts/lib/speech.py`. **Investigation overturned the original "just install torchcodec" plan**: (1) venv is torch 2.8.0+cu128/py3.12 and available torchcodec wheels start at 0.7.0 (ABI-matched to a different torch — mismatch risks breaking the torch the whole pipeline needs); (2) `C:\ffmpeg\bin` is a STATIC FFmpeg build with no `av*.dll`, which torchcodec requires — so install would fail at runtime anyway; (3) it'd buy nothing since Stage 2 pre-extracts audio to WAV and `soundfile`/`torchaudio` (both present) decode that perfectly. The pyannote fallback is the *correct* path here. **Fix**: a regex-scoped `warnings.filterwarnings("ignore", message=r"(?s).*torchcodec is not installed correctly", category=UserWarning)` at the top of speech.py — silences ONLY that benign one-time UserWarning (the `(?s)` crosses the message's leading newline), not a blanket ignore. Unit-verified it suppresses that exact message while letting unrelated UserWarnings through; module compiles clean. Diarization coverage unchanged (4621/4706). Pages: [[concepts/clip-quality-remediation-2026-06]] (Fix 4 SHIPPED), [[entities/diarization]].

## [2026-06-06] update | config/models.json context_length 65536 → 32768
Operator dropped `context_length` from 65536 to 32768 (the 2026-06-06 rakai review run was at 64K). 32K is the recommended/workload-aware value: it shrinks `qwen3.6-35b-a3b`'s KV cache → more headroom in the 28.5 GB two-GPU pool, and is still well above the chunked pipeline's ~14K-token peak demand, so no clip-quality loss. Committed the config alongside the wiki note. Pages: [[concepts/vram-budget]] (live-config verification callout), [[index]] indirectly. ## [2026-06-06] query+update | Last-session review + LM Studio 10 GB system-RAM question
Reviewed the most recent clipping session (`20260606_071210_20260424_2xRaKai`, rakai 193-min VOD) and answered the user's "why does LM Studio hold 10 GB system RAM" question. **RAM finding (the big one): the user has TWO GPUs** — NVIDIA RTX 5060 Ti 16 GB + **AMD Radeon RX 6700 XT 12 GB** (combined pool 28583 MB), and LM Studio splits `qwen3.6-35b-a3b` (22 GB) across both via the Vulkan backend ("split evenly"). The per-stage `[VRAM]` telemetry proves it: during Stage 4 the pool showed **24116/28583 MB used = 13.4 GB on NVIDIA + 10.8 GB on AMD**, both with free headroom. So the model is **fully resident in VRAM, NOT spilling to system RAM**. The ~10 GB system-RAM working set is the **mmap'd GGUF file (page cache) + Vulkan host-staging buffers** — reclaimable/benign, not on the compute hot path. The real (modest) perf cost is Vulkan cross-vendor split being slower than CUDA-on-one-card; a model that fits the 16 GB NVIDIA card alone (qwen3.5-9b 6.5 GB or gpt-oss-20b 12 GB @ 32K) would run CUDA-native and faster, at a quality tradeoff. **Verified working** (prior plans): arc-aware extraction (25 cards/5 arcs — see [[concepts/arc-aware-extraction]]), VRAM observability, audio-events `parallel x8` @ 5.2 win/s (vs 1.7 pre-fix), M1 diarization, M3 callbacks, segment detection (12 segments), model-split same-model swap skip, force-reprocess re-transcribe. Last 4 rakai runs all exit 0 / 10 clips. **Bugs found**: (1) [[concepts/bugs-and-fixes#BUG 60]] vestigial `\`-backtick fence-strip in `stage6_vision.py:542-543` (FIXED this session; stage4 was already fixed) — contributes to vision REGEN; (2) repeated vision grounding REGEN failures → some clips ship fallback titles like "Pattern setupexternalcontradiction Streamer claims" (NOT yet fixed — vision-grounding-strictness investigation); (3) `torchcodec not installed` → diarization on fallback decoder; (4) Pass C score saturation (all 10 finals pinned at 1.000); (5) Vision Judge tournament (Stage 5.5) = 620s/58min — big cost. Pages: [[concepts/bugs-and-fixes]] (BUG 60), [[concepts/arc-aware-extraction]] (production verification), [[index]].

## [2026-06-06] update | Implemented arc-aware extraction Phases 1+2 (chunk cards + grouped-register A1)
Implemented the full [[concepts/arc-aware-extraction]] plan (Phases 1 & 2) in `scripts/lib/stages/stage4_moments.py`, replacing the 15-word per-chunk summary that fed Tier-3 A1 cross-chunk arc detection. **Phase 1** — added `chunk_cards` dict + 5 helpers: `_arc_extract_json_obj` (fence-strip + outermost-`{...}` JSON parse), `_arc_verify_quotes` (substring-verify each quote against the chunk, whitespace-normalized/case-insensitive/≥3 chars, list-capped 3/2/5/2), `_build_chunk_card` (one `call_llm` per chunk → `{topic,claims,predictions,entities,open_loops}`, `max_tokens=4000` reused, `max_retries=0`, non-fatal), `_card_to_oneliner` (flatten → `chunk_summaries` so Tier-1 Q1 prior-context is unchanged), `_build_arc_register` (type-grouped register). The per-chunk summary block now builds a card, stores it, and falls back to first ~12 transcript words if extraction fails. **Phase 2** — A1 global pass now prefers the type-grouped register (`== CLAIMS / PREDICTIONS / OPEN LOOPS / TOPICS ==`, counters Lost-in-the-Middle), falls back to the flat skeleton when no cards exist; A1 prompt rewritten to "Match on MEANING, not shared words". `{"arcs":[…]}` contract + validation + 1.4× boost unchanged.
