Left as the user set it — their choice. No code touched; logging the config state per the wiki-update rule.

## [2026-06-06] query | A1 15-word-summary sufficiency assessment + arc-aware-extraction research plan
User asked (review only) whether the 15-word per-chunk summary feeding Tier-3 A1 cross-chunk arc detection is enough, then asked to save the assessment + research a plan. **Assessment** (filed to [[concepts/two-stage-passb]] §Evaluation): 15 words is a ~77:1 compression that systematically discards the *minor-at-the-time* setups arcs hinge on. Handles theme-level/dominant-thread arcs fine, but structurally fails on (1) buried minor setups (the canonical penthouse brag inside a chunk about something else — the summarizer's "keep the MAIN topic" instruction filters out exactly the un-main detail that pays off), (2) specific entities genericized away ("Delaware"→"rap battle"), (3) multi-topic chunks where only one thread survives. M3 (callbacks) backstops *lexically-similar* callbacks (it embeds real transcript, not summaries) but misses *low-similarity conceptual/ironic* arcs — the residual gap, which is exactly A1's stated specialty. It's a tradeoff not a clean bug (A1 is boost-only; terser skeleton is easier to scan — Lost-in-the-Middle). **Research** (general-purpose agent, adversarially verified): recommends replacing the free-text 15-word summary with a fixed-size structured "chunk card" {topic, claims[], predictions[], entities[], open_loops[]} (~60-80 tokens) grounded in Chain-of-Density (Adams 2023, entity-dense fixed-length) + committed-belief/claim extraction (FactBank), and feeding A1 a type-grouped register (not a prose blob) to counter Lost-in-the-Middle (Liu 2023). Critical verified nuance: constrain the JSON *emission*, NOT the *reasoning* ("Let Me Speak Freely?" EMNLP 2024 — reasoning inside strict JSON costs 10-15%). Substring-verify quotes against the chunk to kill hallucinations. **Plan filed** as new page [[concepts/arc-aware-extraction]] — techniques table, recommended card schema + grouped-register A1, prompt sketches for 9-35B Q4, risk table, 4-phase plan (instrument → swap extractor → grouped register → measure precision via judge_tournament/axis_report), with the decision rule "keep only if buried-setup recall rises WITHOUT arc-clip win-rate falling." Cost: same call count, ~2-4× output tokens on the one per-chunk summary call, zero added VRAM. **No code changed** — assessment + plan only. Pages: created [[concepts/arc-aware-extraction]]; updated [[concepts/two-stage-passb]] (§Evaluation), [[concepts/moment-discovery-upgrades]] + [[index]] (links).

## [2026-06-06] query | Verifying VRAM fit via `lms load --estimate-only`; 64K vs 32K on the 35b
User asked whether 65K context beneficially upgrades 32K, how to verify if 65K leaks layers into system RAM, and whether to test-run first. **Verified on hardware** with `lms load <model> -c <ctx> --estimate-only` (non-destructive — does NOT load): qwen3.6-35b-a3b @ 32K → 22.24 GiB GPU; @ 64K → 23.30 GiB; @ 256K → 29.66 GiB (exceeds the 27.9 GiB pool → spills). **Answers**: (1) 64K gives NO functional benefit over 32K — the chunked pipeline's peak per-call demand is ~14K tokens, so 32K already has 2× headroom; 64K just reserves ~1 GiB more KV for nothing. (2) For the 35b, 64K does NOT spill (23.3 < 27.9 pool), but effective free pool is ~25 GiB after the desktop/busy-browser baseline (~2.9 GiB), so 64K's ~1.7 GiB margin is thinner than 32K's ~2.8 GiB → 32K is safer. (3) No full test run needed for fit — `--estimate-only` confirms it instantly; only run one to measure real speed (watch logtool vram + Pass B chunk timings). **Key findings recorded**: `lms load --estimate-only` is the authoritative per-machine fit check — read "Estimated GPU Memory" vs physical pool, and IGNORE the "may be loaded based on guardrails" line (it prints even when over-budget). Also discovered `model_registry`'s FP16 KV math is CONSERVATIVE vs LM Studio's actual — it projected ~27.4 GiB for the 35b @ 64K where LM Studio reported 23.3 GiB (LM Studio uses a more efficient/quantized KV cache, likely the "Unified KV Cache" option that was enabled). So the tool under-states fittable context (safe direction); trust `--estimate-only` for the final word. **Recommendation to user: set 32K.** Pages: added "Verifying fit on real hardware" section to [[concepts/vram-context-tooling]]. No code/config changes this turn.

## [2026-06-06] query | Engine/GPU control investigation + VRAM-context-tooling consolidation page
User asked whether the project can force CUDA-only (their LM Studio is dual-GPU Vulkan, "split evenly"), then directed: don't pursue CUDA-forcing — keep the tooling **engine-agnostic**, driven only by predicted context length + the pipeline's actual usage, for whatever engine/GPU/CPU the user runs. **Investigated `lms` CLI GPU control** (read-only): `lms load --gpu <ratio>` is offload-ratio only (GPU vs CPU), NOT GPU/engine selection; `lms runtime ls` shows installed engines (dev box: `llama.cpp-win-x86_64-vulkan-avx2@2.20.1 ✓` selected, CUDA engines installed but unselected); `lms runtime select <alias>` switches the GLOBAL engine but there's no per-API-call backend control. **Confirmed**: the project (HTTP API + `lms load` only) cannot set backend, GPU strategy, or per-model GPU placement — those are LM Studio app/GUI/runtime settings. **Decision recorded**: stay engine-agnostic — recommendation is pool-VRAM + workload driven, takes whatever engine/GPU layout the operator chose as given; `cuda_single_card_fits` is informational only, not a backend push. **Created** [[concepts/vram-context-tooling]] — a detailed hub page consolidating this session's whole VRAM/context subsystem: the 4 pieces (vram_log cross-vendor snapshot, gguf_meta exact KV reader, model_registry predictions/recommendations, logtool vram + dashboard endpoint), the GGUF-exact-vs-heuristic correction table (gemma 11×, gpt-oss 2×), the workload-aware design decision (32K not max-fits), portable models-root discovery, the engine-control findings, and the quant audit. **Fixed stale content in** [[entities/lm-studio]]: removed the old flat-rate KV table (wrong up to 11×), rewrote the GPU-configuration section into an operator-controlled/project-agnostic control matrix with the `lms runtime`/strategy findings. **Note**: user is actively experimenting with config/models.json (qwen3.5-9b ↔ qwen3.6-35b-a3b, context 32K/64K/128K) — that's expected; the recommendation tooling guides those choices. Pages: created [[concepts/vram-context-tooling]]; updated [[entities/lm-studio]] (KV table + GPU/engine section + related), [[index]] (both vram pages). No code changes this turn — investigation + documentation only.

## [2026-06-06] update | Context recommendation made workload-aware (was recommending the max-that-fits, which is overkill)
User asked how a large context window affects clip judging / cross-chunk inference, especially for a small model that CAN hold a large context — "is too much overkill like reserving too much RAM?" **Answer: yes, and it actively hurts.** Verified the pipeline is architecturally chunked — peak per-call context demand is ~14K tokens (Pass B worst case: ~6K prompt + up to 8K generation); even the whole-stream Tier-3 A1 cross-chunk arc pass uses only ~30-60 summary lines (~3KB, per the code comment at stage4_moments.py:1697). Cross-chunk inference is done via the summary-skeleton mechanism, NOT raw context. So 16K is the floor, 32K is comfortable, nothing benefits from more. **The flaw**: my `recommend_context` (shipped afe8591) returned the LARGEST context that fits the pool — so it told the user "128K right-sized" for qwen3.5-9b. But 128K reserves 16 GB of KV cache that Pass B fills only 4.6% of, AND pushes the 6.5 GB qwen3.5-9b onto the slower Vulkan pool (22.8 GB > 16 GB CUDA) when at 32K it fits the fast CUDA single card (10.8 GB). **Fix**: added `WORKLOAD_FLOOR_CONTEXT=16384` / `WORKLOAD_COMFORT_CONTEXT=32768`; `recommend_context` now returns `recommended` = workload-optimal (min of 32K, native, max-fits) PLUS `max_fits` (the capability ceiling) PLUS `cuda_single_card_fits` (does the model at the recommended context stay on the fast single card). Added a `cuda_card_mb` param threaded from the endpoint (NVIDIA card size). `recommend_context_combo` surfaces all of it. **Dashboard**: the recommendation line now explains "32K covers the chunked workload (peak ~14K tokens); could hold up to {ceiling} but the pipeline never uses it — larger just reserves unused KV cache", a ⚡ CUDA-fast-path note when applicable, and flags when the current setting is "overkill — reserves KV cache the pipeline never uses". **logtool vram** table reworked: `rec ctx` / `ceiling` / `CUDA@rec` columns (qwen3.5-9b shows rec=32K, ceiling=131K, CUDA@rec=⚡yes). Pages: [[concepts/vram-budget]] (new "Why bigger context ≠ better clips" section with the per-call demand table + the qwen3.5-9b 32K-vs-128K backend tradeoff). Files: `scripts/lib/model_registry.py` (workload constants + reworked recommend_context/combo), `dashboard/routes/models_routes.py` (pass cuda_card_mb), `dashboard/static/modules/models-panel.js` (render workload_note + cuda_note + ceiling), `scripts/logtool.py` (rec/ceiling/CUDA@rec columns). node --check validates the JS; all CLIs verified.

## [2026-06-05] update | Deterministic KV-cache (GGUF metadata) + dashboard context recommendation
Follow-up to the VRAM observability work: replaced the heuristic per-architecture KV-cache rate table with **exact values read from each model's GGUF header**, and wired a GPU-aware context recommendation into the dashboard. **The honesty correction**: the earlier KV rates were formula-estimates from representative architecture params, NOT measured — my code comment claiming they were "verified against LM Studio" was an overstatement. Reading the actual GGUF metadata (block_count, head_count_kv, key_length, value_length, sliding_window_pattern) exposed large errors: gpt-oss-20b was +98% over, gemma-4-12b was **+1010% over** (11×!) because Gemma's sliding-window attention caps 40 of 48 layers at a 1024-token window — the flat-rate heuristic treated all layers as full-attention. Consequence: the old tool wrongly said gemma-4-12b fit only 16K context on a 16 GB card; the exact math says it fits the full 256K native. **New module** `scripts/lib/gguf_meta.py` — minimal GGUF header parser (reads only the KV block, ~5-20ms even on a 22 GB file), exposes `kv_cache_bytes(meta, context)` with proper SWA handling, `native_context()`, `summarize()`. Standalone CLI `python scripts/lib/gguf_meta.py <path.gguf> --context 32768`. **Rewrote** `scripts/lib/model_registry.py` — now discovers the LM Studio models root portably (env `CLIP_LMSTUDIO_MODELS_DIR` → cache/lmstudio defaults → drive-root scan for `\lm-studio`; found `G:\lm-studio` on the dev box), maps lms model IDs → GGUF paths via normalized substring match, uses gguf_meta for exact KV with the heuristic table as fallback, and `recommend_context` walks context tiers from largest-fitting. New `recommend_context_combo(text, vision, pool)` returns the shared context for split configs (more-constrained model wins; consolidation = single model). **Dashboard**: `/api/models/context-recommendation` endpoint (dashboard/routes/models_routes.py) takes text+vision models + live pool, returns recommended context + CUDA-only caveat; models-panel.js `fetchContextRecommendation()` fires on every model dropdown change and renders a "💡 Recommended context: 64K … [Apply]" line under the Context Window card; `applyRecommendedContext()` sets the dropdown. app.js exposes both to window for the inline onclick. **Verified on dev box**: pool 28583 MB, qwen3.6-35b-a3b consolidation recommends 65536 (currently configured 32768 — could double it); gemma-4-12b CUDA-only jumped 16K→256K after the SWA fix. logtool vram KV-source column now shows gguf vs heuristic per model (also fixed a cosmetic bug where that column printed the arch name). Pages updated: [[concepts/vram-budget]] (top callout rewritten, new "KV-cache: deterministic from GGUF" subsection with the error table, per-model KB/tok table corrected, Gemma context-dependent-rate note). Files: `scripts/lib/gguf_meta.py` (new ~230 lines), `scripts/lib/model_registry.py` (rewritten ~430 lines), `scripts/logtool.py` (KV-source column fix), `dashboard/routes/models_routes.py` (+70 lines endpoint), `dashboard/static/modules/models-panel.js` (+115 lines recommendation UI), `dashboard/static/app.js` (+2 window exports). Node --check validates the JS.

## [2026-06-05] update | Cross-vendor VRAM observability — NVIDIA + AMD, per-stage trajectory, model-fit recommendations
Shipped a full GPU/VRAM observability stack that works across both NVIDIA (via `nvidia-smi`) and AMD on Windows (via PowerShell `Get-Counter '\GPU Adapter Memory(*)\Dedicated Usage'` for used MB + registry `HardwareInformation.qwMemorySize` for totals). The PowerShell + registry path was the load-bearing question — verified working: NVIDIA RTX 5060 Ti reports 16311 MB total, AMD RX 6700 XT reports 12272 MB, both detected in a single ~3s probe.
**Three new files**: (1) `scripts/lib/vram_log.py` — cross-vendor snapshot module with `snapshot()`, `stage_snapshot(stage_label, work_dir)`, and standalone CLI `python scripts/lib/vram_log.py --snapshot`. Adapter-counter pairing uses descending-size sort heuristic (works reliably for distinct-VRAM cards). Failure-soft via try/except — pipeline keeps running if nvidia-smi or PowerShell are missing. (2) `scripts/lib/model_registry.py` — parses `lms ls` text output into structured records (id, params, arch, size_mb), with a per-architecture KV cache rate table (Qwen 3.5/3.6 dense ~130 KB/tok, MoE ~105 KB/tok, Gemma 4 ~390 KB/tok due to 256-dim head_dim, gpt-oss ~95 KB/tok, nemotron hybrid ~60 KB/tok). Exposes `predict_vram(model, ctx)` and `recommend_context(model, available_pool_mb, safety_mb=500)`. Tier-snaps to {4K, 8K, 16K, 32K, 64K, 128K, 256K}. (3) `scripts/logtool.py` `cmd_vram` — three-section view: live adapter summary, per-stage trajectory from last run's `vram_log.json`, recommended context per installed LLM for both CUDA-single-card and Vulkan-pool fit modes. ANSI color coding for fit_class (green=easy, yellow=tight, red=spill risk).
**Pipeline hook**: `scripts/pipeline/common.py::set_stage()` now calls `vram_log.stage_snapshot()` so every stage transition snapshots VRAM. Adds ~3s per stage on first call (PowerShell startup), ~500ms on subsequent calls. Net cost: ~10s extra per pipeline run for full trajectory.
**Cross-validation against current dev box**: 28583 MB pool detected, qwen3.6-35b-a3b recommended at 32K context (fits_easily with 5183 MB headroom for KV cache after 22600 MB weights + 300 MB overhead + 500 MB safety). Matches the user's current `config/models.json` setting exactly.
**Wiki updates**: [[concepts/vram-budget]] now has (a) a top-of-page success callout describing the new instrumentation + APIs, (b) refreshed per-model VRAM table with KV-cache rates and native max contexts, (c) new "Per-stage max_tokens" section documenting all 11 LLM call sites with their output-token budgets and explaining they're output-side (not context-bound) but require `context_length ≥ prompt + max_tokens`, (d) new "Portable hardware → recommended config" table covering 8/12/16/24/28 GB scenarios for other users cloning the repo. Files: `scripts/lib/vram_log.py` (new, ~290 lines), `scripts/lib/model_registry.py` (new, ~330 lines), `scripts/logtool.py` (+140 lines `cmd_vram` + helpers + subparser), `scripts/pipeline/common.py` (+8 lines hook into set_stage). Verified end-to-end: live snapshot picks up both cards, recommendations match `config/models.json`, logtool vram renders 3 clean sections.

## [2026-06-05] query | Post-run review of the 17:06 rakai run — 5 findings + BUG 60
Reviewed the 2026-06-05 17:06 rakai run (commits up to `2e4aca8`, all rounds 1-4 + BLAS-pin + audio fast-load shipped pre-run). Five non-blocking observations + a new bug:

**(1) BUG 60 — Stage 6 vision leaks `Pattern <id>:` reasoning text into title/description**. Observed on T=7749 (title `Pattern socialcallout Friend roasts streamer for l`) and T=9985 (description starts with `Pattern social_callout:`). Filed as [[concepts/bugs-and-fixes]] §BUG 60 with diagnosis + fix sketch (regex strip in stage6_vision.py post-process + prompt-side prohibition). Selection-neutral quality fix.

**(2) Axis global clamp bound 253/253 candidates** — per-axis ceilings produce a natural product that exceeds the [0.8, 1.35] global clamp on every Pass C candidate. Compounds with the Delaware rare-pattern issue: candidates that don't activate axes get crushed by candidates that hit the ceiling. Either lower per-axis ceilings, raise the clamp, or add pattern-aware compensation (Phase 2). The `logtool selection` tool will show the per-axis breakdown for empirical tuning.

**(3) Chat features disabled** for the rakai VOD (no `vods/.chat/...jsonl`, auto-fetch off). Degrades Pass A hard-events, Pass B chat context, Stage 6 sub/raid/donation grounding, and Pass C engagement axis. Not a bug; suggested follow-up is a dashboard auto-fetch checkbox.

**(4) Stage 7 render under-scaled** — 412.9 s for 10 clips with `STAGE7_WORKERS=4` = only 1.6× over serial (predicted 3-4×). Likely ffmpeg-internal threading colliding with worker-level parallelism on the 24-core CPU. Tuning candidates: `STAGE7_WORKERS=6` (oversubscribed), or `=3` with each ffmpeg bound to `-threads 8` (sums to 24).

**(5) Pass B per-chunk timing steady at ~37 s/chunk** — qwen3.6-35b-a3b MoE thinking-off on Vulkan pool delivers consistent throughput, no slow-chunk outliers from BUG 20-class issues. With per-chunk cost so low, the deferred parallel HTTP would still save ~12 min but is no longer dominant.

**(6) Grounding regen fired 4/10 final clips (40%)** — tier-3 cascade catching ungrounded fields on first VLM pass. Many likely fixing the same pattern-text leak from BUG 60; the BUG 60 fix may also lower regen rate.

All five logged to [[concepts/pipeline-optimizations-2026-06]] §"Observations from the 2026-06-05 17:06 rakai run". Next-session priority list at the end of that section: BUG 60 fix → verify BLAS-pin & fast-load → verify `logtool selection` → Phase 2 rare-pattern → Stage 7 tuning → chat auto-fetch toggle. No code changes — analysis and documentation only.

## [2026-06-05] update | audio_events fast-load path — soundfile.read + polyphase resample
The same rakai run that surfaced the BLAS-pin issue also measured the audio load at **53 s** for a 3.2 h 16 kHz WAV (977 MB output). Root cause: `librosa.load()` defaults to `res_type="kaiser_best"` which is the highest-quality resampler but ~5-7× slower than `scipy.signal.resample_poly`. For HPSS / onset / RMS detection the quality difference is inaudible; speed dominates. Fix: new `_load_audio_fast()` helper in `scripts/lib/audio_events.py` does `soundfile.read(dtype="float32", always_2d=False)` → optional mono mix-down → `librosa.resample(res_type="polyphase")`. Wrapped in try/except so any non-OOM failure falls back to the original `librosa.load` for codec compatibility. MemoryError propagates to the same OOM handler from either path. The `[AUDIO_EVENTS] loaded …` log line now reports `method=soundfile+polyphase` or `method=librosa.load` so the operator can confirm which path ran. Skips resampling entirely when source already matches target rate (common when an operator pre-extracts at 22050 Hz). **Expected**: 53 s → ~7-10 s on the same rakai input. Combined with the BLAS-pin fix earlier today, Tier-2 M2 wall-clock projection drops from 11.6 min (observed) to under ~3 min on a 3 h VOD. Pages updated: [[entities/audio-events]] (fast-path success callout). Files: `scripts/lib/audio_events.py` (+50 lines `_load_audio_fast` helper + 20 lines wrapping the call). Smoke test scheduled to run on the existing `work/audio.wav` to verify speedup + result parity.

## [2026-06-05] update | audio_events parallelism BLAS-pinning fix — closes the 8-worker scaling gap
First production run with the parallel audio_events path (2026-06-05 16:08-16:19, rakai re-run) showed the multiprocessing was running (``backend=librosa+mp8``) but **scaling poorly**: 1.7 win/s with 8 workers = only 2.1× speedup over the 0.8 win/s serial baseline (expected 6-8×). Total scan took 11.6 min on a 3.2 h VOD when it should have been ~2-3 min. **Root cause**: NumPy's BLAS library (which librosa's HPSS STFT calls into) defaults to spawning ``cpu_count`` threads. On the i9-13900K (24 cores) with 8 worker processes, each worker tried to use all 24 cores for its BLAS ops → 8 × 24 = 192 BLAS threads competing for 24 cores → massive context switching and cache thrashing. **Fix**: ``scripts/lib/audio_events.py::_worker_init`` now sets 5 BLAS thread env vars (``OMP_NUM_THREADS``, ``OPENBLAS_NUM_THREADS``, ``MKL_NUM_THREADS``, ``NUMEXPR_NUM_THREADS``, ``VECLIB_MAXIMUM_THREADS``) to ``1`` BEFORE importing NumPy. Critical timing: NumPy caches the BLAS thread count on first import of ``numpy.linalg``; later changes are ignored. Uses ``setdefault`` so operator can override via env. Expected result: 8 workers run truly in parallel on dedicated cores → 6-8 win/s = the original 8× target. Verified: AST OK; env-var setup confirmed to occur BEFORE the NumPy import (offset 1651 vs 1867 in the function body). Real-world verification requires next pipeline run. Pages updated: [[entities/audio-events]] (BLAS-pinning success callout added before multiprocessing callout). Files: ``scripts/lib/audio_events.py`` (+25 lines of fix + extensive comment explaining why before-import timing matters).

Will reproduce on the next real run before shipping. ## [2026-06-04] update | Structural FN fix: Pass A keyword expansion + pattern catalog markers + cached-transcript audio recovery
After noting that the round-2 dead-chunk gate amplified false negatives that already existed structurally (Pass A keyword vocabulary gaps, Pass B prompt template gaps for pattern types like rap_battle_freestyle, cached-transcript path didn't extract audio.wav so audio_events silently disabled), shipped the three "quick wins" from the case-rap-battle-missed proposal. **(A) Pass A keyword expansion** in `KEYWORD_SETS` (stage4_moments.py): +12 rap-battle / freestyle / verbal-duel phrases to "dancing", +6 social_callout phrases to "controversial", +8 interview_revelation phrases to "storytime". Conservative selection (3+ word phrases or unmistakeable context) to avoid false positives. Verified single dict, no duplicate keys (caught and fixed a duplicate-key bug mid-edit), AST OK. **(B) Pattern catalog enhancement** in config/patterns.json: the rap_battle_freestyle pattern signature was audio-centric and silently failed on text-only LLMs; added TRANSCRIPT MARKERS the LLM can use when audio backend signal is unavailable (≥3 consecutive end-rhymes in ~20s; call-and-response + metered punchline; hype-shout loop; clusters of short metered sentences). Added rhythmic_speech>=0.7 and end_rhyme_chain to structural signals + worked example using the Delaware transcript itself. **(C) Cached-transcript audio recovery** in scripts/pipeline/stages/stage2.py: the cached-transcript branch now extracts audio.wav from the source VOD before the Tier-2 M2 scan. Pre-fix, cached re-runs wrote `{"skipped_reason": "no_audio_source"}` and silently disabled rhythmic_speech / crowd_response / music_dominance — one of the three failures stacked behind the Delaware miss. Net: the rakai Delaware rap battle should now be detectable on a fresh run because (a) Pass A surfaces keyword matches in the chunk → drives cross-validation, (b) Pass B has explicit transcript markers to recognize, (c) audio_events fires rhythmic_speech ≥0.7 confirming the pattern. **Dashboard label update**: Pass B gate dropdown labels now lead with predicted speed increase rather than jargon — "Off (default) — 0% faster, safest" / "Multi — ~10% faster, very low FN risk" / "Sample — ~22% faster, low FN risk" / "Strict — ~28% faster, FN-prone (legacy)". Pages updated: [[concepts/case-rap-battle-missed]] (items 1-3 marked SHIPPED with concrete implementation notes). Files: `scripts/lib/stages/stage4_moments.py`, `config/patterns.json`, `scripts/pipeline/stages/stage2.py`, `dashboard/templates/index.html`. Items 4-6 (phonetic rhyme-density signal, per-segment local windows, diarization-driven verbal-duel detector) remain as documented future work — those are architectural changes that need eval coverage.

## [2026-06-04] update | Pipeline optimization round 4 — Pass B dead-chunk gate redesigned (multi-signal + sampling + audit log)
After noting the false-negative risk of the round-2 dead-chunk pre-filter (per the rakai Delaware case study: 2-signal gate has ~5-10% false negatives, which compound with Pass C's competitive bucket selection — a missed clip displaces a worse one rather than just disappearing), redesigned the gate as a four-mode configurable system. **Modes** (`CLIP_PASSB_DEAD_GATE` env): `off` (new default, no filtering, zero false negatives), `strict` (round-2 2-signal behaviour, deprecated as default), `multi` (6 signals: keywords + audio_events + chat hard-events + diarization speakers ≥2 + word density ≥1.5/sec + segment type in {reaction, hot_take, just_chatting}), `sample` (multi + every Nth dead chunk LLM'd anyway, bounds consecutive-skip streak). **Round-4 verification**: 5 of 6 signals were already loaded at chunk-loop scope (`keyword_moments`, `AUDIO_EVENTS`, `CHAT_FEATURES.window()`, per-segment `speaker` from diarization, `seg_type`); only word density is computed inline. **Audit log**: `{TEMP_DIR}/pass_b_skipped_chunks.json` written every run (even with zero skips — a positive signal). New `logtool dead` subcommand renders the skip table with per-row signal breakdown for post-run audit. **Legacy compat**: `CLIP_PASSB_KEEP_DEAD_CHUNKS=1` still honoured as alias for `off`. **Trade-off matrix**: off (0% lift / no FN risk) → multi (5-15% lift / very low FN risk) → sample (20-25% lift / low FN risk) → strict (25-30% lift / meaningful FN risk). Default-off keeps current behaviour selection-safe; operators opt into faster modes deliberately. Pages updated: [[concepts/pipeline-optimizations-2026-06]] (§4 Pass B gate section rewritten; env-var quick-ref updated). Files changed: `scripts/lib/stages/stage4_moments.py` (gate rewritten + 6-signal logic + audit log write at end-of-loop), `scripts/logtool.py` (new `cmd_dead` + subparser + dispatch). Verified: AST OK on both; `logtool dead` smoke-tested against synthetic skip-log data.

## [2026-06-04] update | Pipeline optimization round 3 — Stage 6 vision parallel HTTP (selection-neutral)
Implemented the deferred Stage 6 vision parallelization (item B from the round-2 deferred list). Refactored the 600-line `for moment in moments:` loop in `scripts/lib/stages/stage6_vision.py` into a module-scope `_process_moment(moment) -> entry` function and replaced the loop with `ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=STAGE6_WORKERS).map(_process_moment, moments)`. Order is preserved (`pool.map` yields in submission order); the final `enriched.sort()` doesn't care either way. **Thread safety**: added `threading.Lock` (`_VISION_NET_FAIL_LOCK`) around the `_VISION_NET_FAIL_STREAK` counter mutations inside the nested `_vision_call` closure to avoid read-modify-write races on the circuit-breaker. The "3 consecutive failures" semantic loosens to "3 since last success" under concurrency — still the right behaviour when LM Studio is genuinely down. **Knobs**: `STAGE6_WORKERS` env var; default 2 (conservative for VLM image-encoder serialization); set to 1 to force serial. **Selection-neutral by construction** — each moment's enrichment is fully independent; no cross-moment state beyond the failure counter. **Expected lift**: 2-3× on Stage 6 (13 min → ~5 min); combined wall-clock target now 135 min → ~75-80 min (~1.7×). **Verification**: AST parse OK (901 lines, +82 from 819); `_process_moment` at module scope (line 185); 1 nested closure (`_vision_call`); 6 return statements; dispatch at line 870 after function def + after `moments` and `enriched` initialization at lines 90/94. Pages updated: [[concepts/pipeline-optimizations-2026-06]] (Stage 6 moved from Deferred §B to Implemented §5; combined-impact table refreshed; STAGE6_WORKERS added to env-var quick-reference). Files changed: `scripts/lib/stages/stage6_vision.py`.

## [2026-06-04] update | Pipeline optimization sweep round 2 — Stage 5/7 parallel ffmpeg + Pass B pre-filter + audio_events RMS gate
Second-round implementation pass on the prioritized pipeline optimizations identified after the audio_events parallelization. **Implemented (4)**: (1) **Audio events RMS gate** — cheap energy check (one numpy reduction) before HPSS; silent windows early-exit; 1.5-3× lift on top of mp; `AUDIO_EVENTS_RMS_GATE=0.01` default, tunable. (2) **Stage 5 frame extraction parallel dispatch** — `ThreadPoolExecutor` over pre-collected (frame_t, out_name) tuples; ~5-10× lift on the 480-720 ffmpeg invocations; `STAGE5_WORKERS=8` default. (3) **Stage 7 render + audio extraction parallel dispatch** — same ThreadPool pattern, 4 concurrent ffmpegs each using ~6 internal threads = 24 cores fully utilized; ~3-4× lift (11 min → ~3-4 min); `STAGE7_WORKERS=4` default. (4) **Pass B dead-chunk pre-filter** — skip LLM call when chunk has zero Pass A keyword hits AND zero Tier-2 audio events; 10-30% chunk-call reduction on gaming-heavy streams; `CLIP_PASSB_KEEP_DEAD_CHUNKS=1` to opt out. **Deferred with detailed implementation paths (6)**: Pass B parallel HTTP (biggest win but 2397-line file with complex state — needs careful refactor), Stage 6 vision parallel HTTP, Stage 5.5 Vision Judge concurrent pairs (needs swiss_tournament modification), Tier-2 modules parallel with Stage 3-4 (needs run_pipeline.py orchestrator refactor), LM Studio speculative decoding (zero code, user-side config), LLM JSON response caching. **Expected combined wall-clock**: 135 min → ~80-85 min (~1.6×) from this round; Pass B parallel HTTP would take it to ~50 min. Pages created: [[concepts/pipeline-optimizations-2026-06]] (hub for all implemented + deferred items + env-var quick-reference + impact estimates). Pages updated: [[entities/audio-events]] (RMS gate success callout added before the mp success callout), [[index]] (pipeline-optimizations-2026-06 added). Code: `scripts/lib/audio_events.py` (+RMS gate helpers), `scripts/pipeline/stages/stage5.py` (rewrite — ThreadPool dispatch), `scripts/pipeline/stages/stage7.py` (ThreadPool over 7b + 7d), `scripts/lib/stages/stage4_moments.py` (+30-line dead-chunk gate inserted after the too-sparse skip). All four files AST-parse and import cleanly.

## [2026-06-04] update | audio_events parallelization implemented (multiprocessing + shared_memory)
Implemented the multiprocessing optimization proposed in the prior query entry. `scripts/lib/audio_events.py` now supports a parallel scan path via `multiprocessing.Pool` + `multiprocessing.shared_memory`: the ~975 MB audio buffer is materialized into shared memory once, workers attach by name (no pickle copies), each imports librosa once at pool startup, and `pool.imap(chunksize=4)` preserves window submission order so the output JSON matches the serial path byte-for-byte. **Tunables** added at the top of the module: `PARALLEL_MIN_WINDOWS=20` (threshold below which serial is faster), `PARALLEL_DEFAULT_CAP=8` (max auto workers), `PARALLEL_CHUNKSIZE=4` (IPC amortization). **Worker count resolution**: explicit arg → `AUDIO_EVENTS_WORKERS` env var → `min(8, cpu_count - 2)`. **CLI flag** `--workers N` (0=auto, 1=force serial, ≥2=that many). **Failure-soft fallback**: if shared-memory creation or pool spawn fails, the serial loop runs as a fallback with `y_full` still in scope. **Backend field** in the output JSON now distinguishes paths (`librosa` vs `librosa+mpN`) so observability shows which path actually ran. **Expected speedup** on i9-13900K: 25 min → ~3-4 min on a 3 h VOD (~8×). Pages updated: [[entities/audio-events]] (success callout replaces the "not implemented yet" note; cost table refreshed with serial vs parallel columns), [[concepts/bugs-and-fixes]] none needed (this is feature work, not a bug fix). Verified: AST parses; module imports clean; auto-resolved worker count = 8 on the i9-13900K. Files changed: `scripts/lib/audio_events.py` (~150 lines added — `_worker_init`, `_worker_run`, `_resolve_worker_count`, `_build_window_tasks`, `_scan_parallel`, refactored `scan_audio_events` to dispatch between serial/parallel).

## [2026-06-04] query | Delaware freestyle case study + audio_events optimization analysis
User asked why a rap battle / freestyle in the 2026-04-24 rakai VOD (T=654-695s, "I'm well aware you're from Delaware") wasn't clipped, and to investigate why the audio_events stage shows no observable CPU/GPU usage despite running ~25 min on a 3 h VOD. **Three-fold diagnosis from `work/` files**: (1) Pass A: 0 keyword moments in the rap-battle window — keyword categories lack rap/freestyle vocabulary. (2) Stage 3: whole VOD classified as 100% "gaming" → Pass B used gaming prompts looking for clutch plays / rage moments / `setup_external_contradiction`; no pattern type for verbal-duel / freestyle. (3) Pass B Chunk 3 (610-910s, covers the rap battle) found 1 moment at T=845 about something else; rap battle not detected. **Bonus finding**: `audio_events.json` was empty with `skipped_reason: "no_audio_source"` — cached-transcript re-runs don't re-extract audio so Tier-2 M2 silently no-ops. **Audio_events performance analysis**: ~0.8 win/s on i9-13900K is single-threaded librosa CPU (HPSS dominant); CPU usage looks invisible because 1 core out of 24 = ~4% total, GPU unused (pure NumPy/SciPy). Multiprocessing pool would give ~8× speedup. Pages created: [[concepts/case-rap-battle-missed]] (new — full case-study + 6 concrete tuning recommendations across Pass A keywords / Pass B prompts / audio_events recovery / phonetic rhyme density / per-segment-type local windows / diarization-driven verbal-duel detector). Pages updated: [[entities/audio-events]] (cost table corrected with measured 0.8 win/s + multiprocessing optimization callout + skipped-reasons table with no_audio_source row), [[index]] (case-rap-battle-missed added). No code/config changed.

## [2026-06-04] update | Qwen 3.6 multimodal discovery — flips the consolidation recommendation
Third-pass research surfaced a major correction. **Qwen 3.6 is multimodal** — both `qwen/qwen3.6-27b` dense AND `qwen/qwen3.6-35b-a3b` MoE. No separate Qwen3.6-VL line; vision is baked in. Confirmed via HF model cards (`image-text-to-text` task class + packaged vision encoder), vLLM Qwen3.5/3.6 recipes doc (vision tower), and Alibaba's published vision benchmarks. The QwenLM GitHub README is misleading (omits vision). **Vision benches for qwen3.6-35b-a3b**: MMMU 81.7 / MMMU-Pro 75.3 / MMBench EN-DEV-v1.1 92.8 / MathVista-mini 86.4 / OmniDocBench 1.5 89.9 / VideoMME w/sub 86.6 — top-of-leaderboard, ahead of Qwen3-VL-30B-A3B on most general benches (Qwen3-VL still wins for documented ScreenSpot 94.7% UI grounding). **Text benches**: MMLU-Pro 85.2 / GPQA 86.0 / AIME 92.7 / LCB v6 80.4 (thinking-on). **Knock-on**: this is plausibly the single best installed model for the entire pipeline — combined with the verified BUG 57 toggle workaround, it becomes the new top consolidation recommendation. **Corrections from earlier research**: OpenAI did NOT publish IFEval for gpt-oss-20b (earlier 65/76 numbers were unsourced secondary derivations); Google did NOT publish IFEval/MMLU-Pro for Gemma 4 12B/26B-A4B/31B (Gemma 3 27B IFEval 90.4 is the anchor); Qwen 3.6 model cards did NOT publish IFEval (Qwen3.5-35B-A3B at 0.919 is the closest proxy). Pages updated: [[entities/qwen35]] (Qwen 3.6 multimodal section added), [[concepts/vlm-comparison-2026-06]] (Qwen 3.6 35B-A3B added as top contender), [[concepts/text-comparison-2026-06]] (benchmark table refreshed with verified Qwen 3.6 + corrections to gpt-oss + Gemma 4), [[concepts/model-split]] (Unified best-models table — Qwen 3.6 35B-A3B promoted to Single-model max-quality consolidation pick). Memory `hardware-specs.md` updated. No code/config changed.

## [2026-06-04] query | Evaluation: Qwen3-VL is OCR-specific (not blanket); MoE+thinking-off is the quality lever
User pushed back on the Qwen3-VL recommendation, CUDA-only, and whether big MoE (few active params) gives better quality. Researched + calibrated (and owned some anchoring): (1) **Qwen3-VL wins OCR** (8B ~96% DocVQA / ~90% OCRBench) but **Gemma 4 leads general visual reasoning** (MMMU-Pro ~77); since the pipeline already runs **PaddleOCR** (BUG 40/41), the VLM OCR edge is partly redundant → Qwen3-VL is a test, not a must-do; installed gemma-4-12b/qwen3.5-9b are fine. (2) **CUDA beats Vulkan on prompt-processing** (~ties on generation); the pipeline is prompt-heavy → CUDA/NVIDIA-only helps for ≤16 GB models (verify on the Blackwell card). (3) **MoE quality = total params, compute = active params** → gemma-4-26b-a4b (~4B active) / qwen3.6-35b-a3b (~3B active) are higher-quality than 9–12B dense at near-small-model compute, and fit the ~28 GB pool. The 35B-A3B's 67-min Stage 4 was the **thinking, not the MoE** — with thinking off it's cheap. Corrected my earlier speed-over-rotation: for the user's *quality* goal, **Tier 2 = a big MoE with thinking off** is likely the sweet spot (test gemma-4-26b-a4b both roles vs the Tier-1 small-dense via `logtool axes`). Pages: [[concepts/model-split]] (Evaluation notes §).

## [2026-06-04] query | Model + thinking research; corrected the dual-GPU VRAM framing
Online research pass on best pipeline models + where to enable thinking. **Thinking verdict: OFF almost everywhere** — external evidence (thinking-mode-in-agent-workflows study + extraction-model research) says reasoning gives little benefit and should be disabled for JSON extraction / classification / summarization / structured output, and the thinking block can exhaust `max_tokens` before answering — the exact failure of **BUG 20**. So: off for Stage 3, Pass B, Pass D, Stage 6; the only thinking-ON candidate is the **Vision Judge** (pairwise judgment). Since the API toggle is ignored (BUG 57), the lever is **model choice** not the flag. **Best per-role:** text (Stage 3 + Pass B + Pass D) → `qwen3.5-9b` (fast) or `gpt-oss-20b`@low (strongest extraction that fits 16 GB), both non-thinking; vision (Stage 6 + Judge) → a **Qwen3-VL** specialist for OCR/grounding (`Qwen3-VL-8B` ~10 GB, or `Qwen3-VL-30B-A3B` MoE ~2.4B active, Q3_K 14 GB fits NVIDIA alone / Q4 18 GB needs the pool) — a worthwhile **download**; `gemma-4-12b` is the no-download fallback. **Correction:** the box also has an **AMD RX 6700 XT (12 GB)** and LM Studio pools **both GPUs via Vulkan ≈ 28 GB**, so the 35B was split across cards in VRAM, **not** CPU-spilling (earlier claim fixed). But fits ≠ fast: Vulkan/both is slower per token than CUDA/NVIDIA-only; models load one-at-a-time (swap per stage) so each gets the full pooled budget. The optimal models all fit the 5060 Ti alone → **CUDA/NVIDIA-only is the fastest path**; reserve Vulkan/both for capacity. Pages: [[concepts/model-split]], [[concepts/vram-budget]], [[concepts/bugs-and-fixes]] (BUG 20/57). Specs memory updated (dual-GPU Vulkan).

## [2026-06-04] update | Model split applied: text=qwen3.5-9b, vision=gemma-4-12b (fit 16 GB; 35B was spilling to CPU)
User applied the recommended split to `config/models.json`: `text_model` qwen3.6-35b-a3b → **qwen/qwen3.5-9b**, `vision_model` → **google/gemma-4-12b** (passb/vision_stage6 stay null → inherit). Motivation surfaced this session: a `logtool axes` review of the 135.8-min run showed **Stage 4 = 67 min (49%)**, caused by two compounding problems with the unified 35B — (1) at **22.1 GB Q4 it exceeds the 16 GB RTX 5060 Ti and spills ~6 GB to CPU** (slow regardless of thinking), and (2) it's a Qwen *thinking* build burning ~3–6k reasoning tokens per Pass B call, with the API `enable_thinking:false` ignored (BUG 57 — only LM Studio's per-model toggle can disable it, uncertainly). The new picks **fully fit 16 GB** (6.5 + 7.6 = 14.1 GB, possibly co-resident → no text↔vision swap): qwen3.5-9b is non-thinking by default (kills the Stage-4 tax) and gemma-4-12b is multimodal. Documented the per-stage thinking map (thinking only helps the Vision Judge + lightly Pass D; Pass B/Stage 3/Stage 6 don't) and the which-installed-models-fit-16 GB table. Specs fetched + saved to agent memory (RTX 5060 Ti 16 GB / i9-13900K / 64 GB). Pages: [[concepts/model-split]] (Active config §), [[concepts/vram-budget]] (current rows + fit note).

## [2026-06-04] update | Per-line + per-VOD log timestamps; reviewed the slow session (Stage 4 = 49%)
**Feature**: `common.Logger` now prefixes **every** log line with `[HH:MM:SS +<elapsed>s]` (`_stamp_lines`, applied in `write()` so it also stamps streamed child-stage output — e.g. per Pass B chunk). Continuation-aware (a partial write + completion is stamped once, not mid-line); stamps only the log copies so `run_module`'s raw `$(...)` capture is untouched; logtool error regexes + the dashboard SSE are mid-line/pass-through so nothing breaks. Added a per-VOD `VOD session time [<vod>]: Xm Ys` line in `run_pipeline._execute_stages` (also covers `--all`). Verified: continuation logic unit-tested + real-Logger smoke test (all lines stamped, none doubled). **Session review** (the user's slow run, `last_run_20260605_005657`, plaqueboymax, 9 clips, **135.8 min**): per-stage timing localized it instantly — **Stage 4 Moment Detection 67.1 min = 49%** (Pass A→D LLM, exploded on the new **35B *thinking* model** `qwen3.6-35b-a3b`), Stage 2 transcription 29.3 (large-v3, pre-turbo), Stage 6 vision 13.0, Stage 7 edit 11.0, Stage 5.5 judge 10.0. Pages: [[concepts/observability]].

## [2026-06-04] update | Whisper large-v3-turbo: downloaded, made the default, added as a dashboard option (+ Windows symlink fix BUG 59)

## [2026-06-04] update | Pipeline observability — axis tuning report, rank churn, stage timing, judge bracket + `logtool axes`
Added post-process visibility for tuning the new A/B/C/E selection axes + the Vision Judge (all read-only, failure-soft). **(1) Axis tuning report** (`stage4_moments.py::_emit_axis_report` → `axis_report.json` + the `[AXES]` log): per-axis coverage (`active`/`pct`), multiplier `min/median/mean/max`, `at_ceil`/`at_floor`, **dependency readiness** (chat/audio/shape loaded?), and `global_clamp.bound_count`. Aggregated over ALL candidates, so a dead axis (missing dependency) is now distinguishable from a neutral one. **(2) Rank churn**: Pass C stamps `base_rank` (pre-multiplier) + `pass_c_rank` (post-axis); the judge stamps `vision_rank` → `base→passC→vision` shows which stage moved a clip. **(3) Per-stage timing** (`common.py::_STAGE_MARKS` via `set_stage` → `stage_timings.json` + a cleanup print), incl. Stage 5.5 separately — the first latency signal for the never-live judge. **(4) Judge pairwise bracket** (`stage5_5_judge.py` `games_log` → `judge_tournament.json`): every comparison's a/b/winner/confidence/reason, even on a partial run. **(5) `logtool axes [RUN]`** renders all four from any past `last_run_*.json`, closing the tune→run→diff loop; the diagnostics dump now keeps the FULL `hype_moments`/`scored_moments` lists (was capped at 30). All modules compile; the 4 axis selftests + judge selftest still PASS; `logtool axes` verified end-to-end on a synthetic snapshot. New page [[concepts/observability]]; touched [[entities/vision-judge]], [[concepts/clipping-intelligence]], index.

## [2026-06-04] update | Fixed BUG 58 — "Force reprocess" now re-transcribes + replaces the cache; cleared transcript cache
Root-caused why pressing "Force reprocess" never re-transcribed: `scripts/pipeline/stages/stage2.py` gated the transcription cache on file existence alone (`if cached_json.exists() and cached_srt.exists():`) and never checked `ctx.force`. The `--force` flag (dashboard → `pipeline_routes.py` → `run_pipeline.py:50`) only drove **Stage 1 VOD selection** (the `processed.log` gate, BUG 1), not the `vods/.transcriptions/` cache — so forced runs always took the cache-hit branch and skipped Whisper. Fix: the cache-hit branch now also requires `not ctx.force`; when forcing, Stage 2 deletes the stale `cached_json`/`cached_srt` (`unlink(missing_ok=True)`), logs the discard, and re-transcribes (the else-branch re-writes the cache → old transcript **replaced**). Non-force caching unchanged. Also **cleared the transcript cache** at the user's request: deleted all 24 files (12 transcripts: `.json`+`.srt`) from `vods/.transcriptions/` for a clean slate before the next run (7 were orphans for VODs no longer on disk; 5 present VODs will re-transcribe). Directory + VOD media untouched. Pages: [[concepts/bugs-and-fixes]] (BUG 58), [[entities/dashboard]].

## [2026-06-04] update | Plan E (engagement/discussion) BUILT — A/B/C/E axis set complete
Built the final selection axis (E-MVP). New `scripts/lib/engagement_signals.py`: surfaces **low-impact but high-engagement** "yap"/take clips via two signals — **predicted** firm-stance (`conversation_shape` `claim_stake`/`info_ramble_marker` WITHOUT an immediate `concession` + a held monologue, kept modest to avoid double-counting the hot_take machinery) and **observed sustained chat discussion** over `[T, T+60]` gated on `unique_chatters` (the genuinely-new signal — deliberately a wider/longer window than Plan B's `[T, T+12]` spike: debate, not a pop). Boost-only ceil 1.12, category-aware, `--selftest` PASS. Wired into Pass C (always-on axis inside the clamped product). Also: an **`engagement` style** in `style_pattern_weights.json` (+ "yap" aliases, `style_prompts`/`weight_map` entries — resolves through `apply_style_weights`, verified); the **`media-pause-commentary`** archetype added to the Stage 6 `interaction_shape` enum (the pause-and-opine pivot the transcript can't see — a prime Vision-Judge signal); `engagement` block in `selection_axes.json`. The discussion-worthiness **judge criterion + card hint are DEFERRED** to the first live judge run (lean-judge-prompt). Diagnostics: `engagement_score`/`engagement_multiplier` + `eng=` in the `[PASS C]` log. **This completes the A/B/C/E Pass-C selection-axis set** (A/B/C/E all live with the global product clamp `[0.80, 1.35]`; ceilings 1.12/1.10/1.18/1.12; D deferred). Highest-priority next step: a live VOD run — the Vision Judge has still never run live. ## [2026-06-04] update | Plan C (baseline-contrast) BUILT — relative-to-self anomaly detection
Built the most novel selection axis. New `scripts/lib/baseline_contrast.py`: `compute_baseline(segments, segment_at, topic_boundaries)` runs ONCE per VOD (speaking-rate mean/std over rolling 30s/10s windows, modal segment-type, flattened topic boundaries) and `evaluate(moment, ...)` scores each moment on **two-sided rate z-deviation** (fast AND slow are breaks) + a **start-aligned topic pivot** (a pivot INTO a topic near the clip start — deliberately NOT a mid-clip crossing, so it does not fight Plan A's crossing penalty) + a **genre shift** (an unusual segment-type for this VOD). Boost-only, cold-start guarded (`min_windows`/`min_rate_std`), orthogonal to the M1 speaker boost. Per the pre-build eval, C is given the **most authority of the axes (ceil 1.18)** as the corrective for energy bias — a quiet beat on a hype streamer can now win. Wired into Pass C: baseline computed before the scoring loop (topic boundaries flattened from `CONVO_SHAPE_INDEX`, modal genre via `get_segment_type`); `axis_mult *= baseline_mult` inside the clamped product; diagnostics `baseline_contrast`/`baseline_multiplier` + `bc=` in the `[PASS C]` log + a one-time `[BASELINE]` line. `--selftest` PASS (fast burst / topic pivot / genre shift all beat typical; degraded + cold-start neutral). Judge criterion deferred (lean-judge-prompt). Config: `baseline_contrast` block in `selection_axes.json`. Pages: [[concepts/clipping-quality-overhaul]], [[concepts/plan-baseline-contrast]], [[concepts/clipping-intelligence]].

## [2026-06-04] update | Pre-build eval of plans A-E + Plan B (reaction-worthy) BUILT
User asked to **review and evaluate plans A-E before implementing**. Verified every load-bearing claim against the code (`chat_features.window`→`z_score`/`unique_chatters` ✓, discourse markers `claim_stake`/`info_ramble_marker`/`concession` ✓, `apply_style_weights` moves `raw_score` while `mmr_rank` does not — confirming D's no-op ✓, the Pass C arc insertion point ✓). Verdict: plans individually sound; the real risk is **emergent** — four axes each doing `styled_score *= mult` uncoordinated (worst-case product ~1.63×, and Pass C ranks on the *uncapped* `raw_score`). Adopted four guardrails: a **global axis-multiplier product clamp `[0.80, 1.35]`**, **rebalanced ceilings** (B smallest at 1.10, C the corrective gets the most), a **lean judge-prompt** (per-axis judge criteria DEFERRED to the first live run), and **D downgraded**. User chose build order **B→C→E** (D deferred). Then **built Plan B**: new `scripts/lib/reaction_signals.py` (boost-only intensity = audio `crowd_response` + post-beat chat-breadth spike gated on `unique_chatters`; category-aware; `--selftest` PASS); refactored Pass C in `stage4_moments.py` to accumulate the A/B axes into one clamped `axis_mult`; added `reaction`+`global` blocks to `config/selection_axes.json`; diagnostics `reaction_score`/`reaction_multiplier`/`axis_multiplier` + `rx=`/`ax=` in the `[PASS C]` log. Dropped the diarized-interruption signal (double-counts M1) and deferred the judge criterion. Pages: [[concepts/clipping-quality-overhaul]], [[concepts/plan-reaction-worthy]], [[concepts/clipping-intelligence]].

## [2026-06-04] plan | Plan D (batch-diversity) implementation plan approved + persisted; latent Phase-4.6 no-op found
Self-evaluated honestly: D is the **lowest-value axis** — Pass C already delivers visible batch diversity (25 s dedup, ≥40 s spacing, time-buckets, ≤50% category cap), so the user has never seen duplicates. Discovered a **latent no-op**: the existing Phase 4.6 MMR (`stage4_diversity.py`, wired `stage4.py:39`) only *reorders* the list and never touches `raw_score`, but the Vision Judge and Stage 6 both re-sort by `raw_score` (`stage6_vision.py:810`) — so its diversity reordering is silently discarded before render. Plan D (reorder-only, per the user's call) right-sizes to: extend `stage4_diversity.py` with `final_diversity_demote` (a bounded/floored `raw_score` demotion via the existing text-MMR helpers + categorical overlap) + a `--final` mode, wire it **post-judge** in `stage6.py`, add a `batch_diversity` config block. No new files, no judge criterion (diversity is a set property). Persisted into the brief; **not yet built**. Pages: [[concepts/plan-batch-diversity]].

## [2026-06-04] plan | Plan C (baseline-contrast) implementation plan approved + persisted
Turned the [[concepts/plan-baseline-contrast]] brief into a concrete, approved implementation plan. Core mechanism (our most novel axis): compute a per-VOD baseline once, then **boost-only** moments that deviate from the streamer's own norm. MVP signals are cheap + already-computed and **orthogonal to the M1 speaker boost** (no double-count): two-sided speaking-rate z-deviation, topic shift (conversation_shape TextTiling boundaries), genre shift (segment-type change). New `scripts/lib/baseline_contrast.py` (`compute_baseline` + `evaluate`, mirrors `arc_completeness.py`); edits to `stage4_moments.py` (one-time baseline + Pass C apply), `vlm_judge.py`/`stage5_5_judge.py` (a "more-surprising-than-this-streamer's-norm" judge criterion + card hint), `config/selection_axes.json`. Audio-loudness RMS + per-segment-type baselines + semantic-drift embeddings deferred to Phase 2. Persisted into the brief; **not yet built** (awaiting go-ahead). Pages: [[concepts/plan-baseline-contrast]].

## [2026-06-04] plan | Plan B (reaction-worthy) implementation plan approved + persisted
Turned the [[concepts/plan-reaction-worthy]] brief into a concrete, approved implementation plan (the agreed A-E flow: brief → impl plan → build). Core design: split reaction *intensity* (a cheap per-moment pre-signal — audio `crowd_response`, chat `z_score`/`burst_factor` + subs/bits floor, diarized interruptions/overlap, **boost-only** ≤~1.20×, mirrors `arc_completeness.py`) from reaction *authenticity* (a new "genuine, earned reaction — avoid forced hype" criterion in the shared [[entities/vision-judge]] prompt + a `[reaction: 0.NN]` card hint). New `scripts/lib/reaction_signals.py`; edits to `stage4_moments.py` (Pass C), `vlm_judge.py`/`stage5_5_judge.py` (judge), `config/selection_axes.json` (reaction block). Facial-expression detector deferred (judge sees faces). Persisted the plan into the brief; **not yet built** (awaiting go-ahead). Pages: [[concepts/plan-reaction-worthy]].

## [2026-06-04] update | Built Phase 1.a — Stage 5.5 Vision Judge (vision finally SELECTS)
The headline change: the multimodal model is promoted from title-writer to selector. Wired into `scripts/pipeline/stages/stage6.py` before vision enrichment (`check=False`, failure-soft: outage / too-few comparisons / timeout all keep Pass C order). `config/judge.json` + `CLIP_JUDGE_CONFIG` (+ `CLIP_SELECTION_AXES_CONFIG`) exported from `paths.child_env`. This is the shared substrate the five selection axes (A-E) plug into. ## [2026-06-04] update | Implemented Plan A — arc-completeness Pass C scorer (first axis goes from brief to code)
New `scripts/lib/arc_completeness.py` scores each moment's structural setup→payoff completeness (opener + resolution + monologue coherence − topic-crossing / mid-thought start) from `conversation_shape` discourse markers + Pattern-Catalog fit → a 0-1 completeness and a gentle, category-aware multiplier (~0.85–1.12) that `stage4_moments.py` Pass C folds into `raw_score`: boost-leaning, **never gates**; arc categories weighted, one-liner (reactive/hype/funny/dancing) categories near-neutral. Tunable via new `config/selection_axes.json`; stamps `arc_completeness`/`arc_multiplier` on each moment for diagnostics + the future Stage 5.5 Vision Judge. Failure-soft (neutral 1.0 if conversation_shape/markers absent). Verified: py_compile + module `--selftest` (complete story ×1.09 vs fragment ×0.96; one-liner near-neutral; degraded path safe) + config resolves on Windows. Deferred to the 1.a substrate: the judge comparison criterion; payoff detection stays proxy-based. Pages: [[concepts/plan-arc-completeness]], [[concepts/highlight-detection]].

## [2026-06-04] query+update | Added engagement / discussion-worthiness as a 5th selection axis (the "yap" / take clip)
User asked whether an engagement metric (vs impact/retention) is feasible/worth it/exists. Researched platform ranking: watch-time/completion dominates distribution but substantive comments are the heaviest-weighted *engagement* signal, driven by relatable opinion/stance — so a low-impact "yap"/take clip can be high-engagement (the quieter genuinely-interesting moments viral-biased selection misses). Mostly new to the pipeline: `chat_features` exists but timing-based chat scoring was removed (we now WANT the latent post-moment discussion), and the Pattern Catalog lacks the pause-and-opine archetype. Filed [[concepts/plan-engagement-discussion]] (Plan E): predicted (LLM discussion-worthiness) + observed (post-moment chat debate density) engagement; two new patterns `media_pause_commentary` (multimodal pause→camera→take, e.g. DDG/Joe Bart) + `topical_take_aside`; niche detection laddered v1 agnostic→v2 category/topic prompt→v3 channel-learned; exposed as both an always-on axis and a selectable "engagement" style. Wired into [[concepts/clipping-quality-overhaul]] (now 5 axes) + [[index]]. Pages: 1 new + 2 updated.

## [2026-06-04] update | Decomposed the selection north star into 4 standalone per-axis sub-plans
The user chose all four "what makes a good clip" axes (stream content varies too much to pick one) and asked for each as a distinct plan a future agent session can research + implement independently; virality dial = light platform-awareness. Created four self-contained briefs: [[concepts/plan-arc-completeness]] (complete self-contained arc), [[concepts/plan-reaction-worthy]] (genuine earned reaction via the multimodal/audio/chat signals selection ignores today), [[concepts/plan-baseline-contrast]] (deviation from the streamer's own norm — our most novel, anomaly-detection mechanism), [[concepts/plan-batch-diversity]] (the delivered set is varied — multimodal MMR). All four compose on the Stage 5.5 Vision Judge as the shared substrate (A/B = judge criteria, C = Pass-A pre-signal, D = post-tournament re-rank). Wired into [[concepts/clipping-quality-overhaul]] + [[index]]. Pages: 4 new + 2 updated.

## [2026-06-04] update | Saved approved clipping-quality overhaul plan + differentiation stance
Researched (web) how commercial AI clippers select/score clips and how Opus Clip's Virality Score is computed (0-99 over Hook/Flow/Value/Trend, opaque weighting, no public validation; creators report it's a noisy sort — low-scored clips often beat high-scored). Saved the approved multi-plan roadmap as [[concepts/clipping-quality-overhaul]] (Plan 1 prompt-only: Stage 5.5 Vision Judge tournament re-rank, arc-driven duration, hook boundaries, viral titles + kinetic captions, visual consistency; Plans 2-4 optional: eval loop → trained reward model → LoRA). Added a **differentiation stance**: borrow commercial *packaging* craft (hooks, captions, sound-off readability) but reject their *selection taste* (opaque virality, trend-chasing, energy-bias) and build our own structure-first + comparative + novelty-aware selection brain. Selection north star being finalized with the user. Pages: [[concepts/clipping-quality-overhaul]] (new), [[index]].

## [2026-06-04] query | Evaluated the clipping prompt engineering + heuristics; documented + archived
Mapped and critically evaluated the full "intelligence layer" end-to-end: segment classification (router) → Pass A keyword scan → Pass B per-chunk LLM (Pattern Catalog) + Pass B-global arcs + Pass B+ callbacks → Pass C multiplicative re-rank + time-bucket distribution → Pass D 7-dim rubric judge → Stage 6 vision enrichment, with the grounding faithfulness cascade running across all generated text. Filed the synthesis + evaluation as a new hub page [[concepts/clipping-intelligence]] (strengths: non-gatekeeping funnel, principled A∩B cross-validation, segment-conditioning, the Pattern Catalog, anti-bias machinery; weaknesses: uncalibrated multiplier chain, correlated same-model "cross-validation" across Pass B/D/vision, brittle substring keywords, 4-way prompt-source drift, unguarded segment classification; opportunities: close the calibration loop via [[entities/bootstrap-twitch-clips]], additive log-space scoring, de-correlate the LLM panel). Froze a source/config snapshot to `archive/clipping-intelligence-2026-06-04/` (+ `.zip`). No code/config behavior changed — read/evaluate/document only. Pages: [[concepts/clipping-intelligence]] (new), [[index]].

## [2026-06-04] update | Logged session findings — BUG 57 (Qwen thinking-leak / empty-content chunk skips)
Reviewing a bare-metal clipping session with `logtool` surfaced the one operational issue worth a dedicated bug entry: qwen3.5-9b (and the 27b) reason on every Pass B call under LM Studio 0.4.14 despite the pipeline's no-think directives, causing slowness and occasional `total_tokens=1` empty responses that skip ~2/15 chunks (handled gracefully — the run still produced 9 clips). Filed as [[concepts/bugs-and-fixes#BUG 57]]; the fix is to disable reasoning in LM Studio's model settings. Everything else from this session (bare-metal migration, lms model management, Whisper/WhisperX + LM Studio interaction docs, logtool, get-models, diarization wiring + validation) was logged incrementally in the entries below. Pages: [[concepts/bugs-and-fixes]].

## [2026-06-04] update | Speaker diarization validated working end-to-end (3 speakers detected)
With a classic Read HF token + terms accepted on all three gated pyannote models (`speaker-diarization-3.1`, `segmentation-3.0`, and pyannote-v4's `speaker-diarization-community-1`), `scripts/validate_diarization.py --full` ran the full `speech.transcribe` path on a 3-minute plaqueboymax sample: WhisperX ASR → wav2vec2 align → pyannote diarize → assign_word_speakers, producing 3 speakers labeled on 77/79 transcript segments in ~5 s of diarization on GPU. Diarization is fully functional; enable on real VODs by re-transcribing (`--force`). Added a `--full` production-path mode to the validator. Pages: [[entities/diarization]].

## [2026-06-04] update | Diarization: fixed whisperx token kwarg + added validate_diarization.py
Implementing/testing Tier-2 M1 diarization on bare metal surfaced two issues. (1) Code bug — whisperx 3.8.6 / pyannote 4.x renamed the auth kwarg `use_auth_token` → `token`; `speech.py::_maybe_diarize` now selects it via signature inspection (works on old + new whisperx). (2) Added `scripts/validate_diarization.py` — downloads the pyannote weights and runs diarization on a short sample as an end-to-end check (uses the authoritative `auth_check`, not `model_info`). Also learned the HF token must be a **classic Read** token (fine-grained tokens 403 on gated repos despite `model_info` reporting OK) with terms accepted on both `pyannote/speaker-diarization-3.1` and `pyannote/segmentation-3.0`. The end-to-end run is still blocked on the user's HF gated access. Pages: [[entities/diarization]].

## [2026-06-04] update | Added logtool.py diagnostics CLI; fixed torchcodec breaking sentence-transformers
Added `scripts/logtool.py` (`doctor` / `list` / `errors` / `show` / `tail`) for triaging run logs in `clips/.pipeline_logs/`. `doctor` is an environment preflight (venv deps incl. torch/CUDA + CTranslate2 cuda devices, ffmpeg, cuDNN DLL dirs, LM Studio reachability + `lms ps` + configured-model availability, paths, disk; non-zero exit on failure). `errors` classifies findings (CRIT/ERR/WARN), attributes each to the stage it occurred in, and filters benign noise. The tool immediately caught a real issue: `torchcodec` 0.7 (needs torch 2.9) fails its DLL load against the pinned torch 2.8.0+cu128 and broke `import sentence_transformers` (Pass B+ callbacks + MMR diversity) — fixed by `pip uninstall -y torchcodec` (noted in `requirements-windows.txt`). Pages: [[concepts/bare-metal-windows]].

## [2026-06-04] update | Documented LM Studio interaction + Whisper/WhisperX transcription in detail
Expanded [[entities/lm-studio]] with the authoritative "Pipeline ↔ LM Studio interaction" spec: HTTP `/v1/chat/completions` inference (payload, reasoning_content fallback, network fail-fast), `GET /v1/models` + the `verify_models` startup gate, the **`lms` CLI** model-lifecycle strategy (per-stage load/unload, the 0.4.14 `/api/v1/models/unload` 404, JIT, `CLIP_MODEL_TTL` idle-evict, skip-if-loaded), and the thinking-model speed lever (27B/35B slow vs 9B fast). Expanded [[entities/faster-whisper]] with how WhisperX (primary: VAD + wav2vec2 alignment) and faster-whisper (fallback) work on bare metal: the two runtimes (CTranslate2 vs PyTorch), the Windows cuDNN/cuBLAS DLL bootstrap, torch 2.8.0+cu128, device/model/cache resolution, output shape, transcription cache, and Stage 7 clip captions. Pages: [[entities/lm-studio]], [[entities/faster-whisper]].

## [2026-06-04] update | Bare-metal Windows migration — Docker removed, bash pipeline ported to Python
Ported the entire system off Docker to native Windows. The bash pipeline (`clip-pipeline.sh` + `pipeline_common.sh` + `stages/*.sh`) is replaced by a pure-Python orchestrator: `scripts/run_pipeline.py` + `scripts/pipeline/common.py` + `scripts/pipeline/stages/stage{1..8}.py`. The reused `scripts/lib/**.py` modules are invoked unchanged via `subprocess.run([sys.executable, ...])`. New `scripts/lib/paths.py` is the single source of truth mapping `/tmp/clipper` and `/root/.openclaw` to Windows dirs; ~14 lib modules parameterized to read those via env vars. Phase 0 validated faster-whisper on the RTX 5060 Ti (Blackwell) via `scripts/validate_gpu.py`; venv uses torch 2.8.0+cu128 + whisperx (gotcha: whisperx pulls CPU torch — reinstall cu128 after). Dashboard runs native (`use_docker_exec()` defaults False; `_state` imports `paths.py` so it reads the live work dir); OpenClaw/Discord run native via `clip.cmd` + `start.ps1`. Docker files moved to `legacy/`. Verified end-to-end through Stage 4 on a cached VOD. Follow-up: model load/unload in `scripts/pipeline/common.py` now uses the bundled `lms` CLI (LM Studio 0.4.14's REST `/api/v1/models/unload` returns 404, stranding models in VRAM — two piled onto the 16 GB GPU) with a `CLIP_MODEL_TTL` idle-evict safety net and skip-if-already-loaded. Pages: [[concepts/bare-metal-windows]], [[overview]], [[concepts/deployment]], [[index]].

## [2026-05-02] update | BUG 56 — Pass C merge keeps wrong peak T, vision titles don't match rendered video

User flagged a clip from the 19:10 run titled "Prom Compliment on the Bus" where the actual rendered footage was "someone missing the bus and everyone reacting." Diagnostic dive on `moment_1179` revealed two distinct moments:

- **Keyword T=1179**: trigger fired on `"Yo... prom coming up... You look very beautiful."`
- **LLM T=1187**: pattern `storytelling_arc` — `"a mini-narrative about Ray missing the bus..."` with `clip_start=1187, clip_end=1212`

8 seconds apart, well within the 25 s Pass C dedup window, so they merged. The merged record kept the keyword's `timestamp=1179` but inherited the LLM's `clip_start=1186.66, clip_end=1212.27` — peak T sat 7.66 s **before** the rendered clip started. Stage 5 frame extraction at `[T-2..T+5]` = `[1177..1184]` ran entirely before the clip, and Stage 6's `T±8s` transcript window pulled the prom dialog from outside the rendered range. Vision dutifully titled the bus footage about prom because that's what it was grounded in.

Three compounding decisions in `scripts/lib/stages/stage4_moments.py`'s merge:
1. No invariant that peak T must stay inside the inherited clip window.
2. The "use LLM's why if score > 0.8 × d" check ran *after* the ×1.25 cross-val boost, so it was effectively dead code — keyword's transcript snippet always won the preview field over LLM's semantic narrative.
3. LLM's `primary_pattern` was never carried into the merged record.

**Fix** (`scripts/lib/stages/stage4_moments.py`):
- Identify the LLM side explicitly in the merge.
- Adopt LLM's `clip_start` / `clip_end` AND, when the existing peak T is outside that window, snap T to the LLM's timestamp.
- Drop the broken 0.8× threshold; always prefer the LLM's `why` for preview/why fields.
- Carry `primary_pattern` and `primary_category` forward from the LLM side.

**Defense in depth** (`scripts/lib/stages/stage6_vision.py`): replaced `local_transcript`'s T±8 window with `[clip_start, clip_end]` (legacy fallback to T±8 if window collapses to <4 s). Vision now grounds against the words actually inside the rendered clip regardless of where peak T sits.

**Verification**: replay of the real T=1179 case through the new merge body asserts (a) peak T snaps 1179 → 1187, (b) `clip_start ≤ T ≤ clip_end` invariant holds, (c) preview/why become the LLM bus narrative, (d) `primary_pattern = storytelling_arc` propagates, (e) cross_validated=True, normalized_score boosts 0.7 → 0.959, (f) Stage 5 frame timestamps `[1185, 1187, 1188, 1189, 1190, 1192]` all fall inside `[1187, 1212]`. AST parse clean on both files.

Pages touched: created [[#BUG 56]] in [[concepts/bugs-and-fixes]] (full symptom/cause/fix + quick-nav row).

## [2026-05-02] update | Three pipeline-log fixes — score saturation, HOOK unbound, Pass D unparseable

User asked to trace errors in the most recent run (`C:\Users\user\AppData\Local\Temp\clipper\pipeline.log`, 2026-05-02 19:10) and asked specifically why every clip displayed `score=1.000` and why the Stage 6 vision boost printed `1.000 -> 1.000`. Three real bugs surfaced.

**BUG 53 — Stage 6 vision boost saturated** (`scripts/lib/stages/stage6_vision.py`). Pass C correctly preserves an uncapped `raw_score` (BUG 37 fix), but Stage 6 was reading the clamped `score` field for its boost math: `1.000 × 1.15 → 1.000`. Fix: read both `score` (display, kept for log compatibility) and `raw_score` (uncapped, used for math). Initialize `entry["raw_score"]` from the moment so vision-skipped/failed entries propagate ranking signal. All three boost paths (`cross_validated_full +0.1`, vision ≥0.67 ×1.15, vision ≥0.44 ×1.08) now operate on raw and clamp only at the display field. FINAL log line now surfaces `raw=` next to `score=` so operators can differentiate clipped-to-1.000 cohort members.

**BUG 54 — `HOOK: unbound variable`** (`scripts/stages/stage7_render.sh:19`). The clip-manifest builder used `python3 -c "..."` (bash double-quoted), and line 44 of the file was a python comment containing `"$HOOK"`. Bash sees `$HOOK` regardless of whether it's inside a python comment, expands it under `set -u`, errors out before python ever runs (HOOK is only bound by the `read -r` loop at line 57). Fix: convert to single-quoted heredoc `python3 - <<'PYEOF'`, which is bash-opaque. Side benefit: removed all the manual `\"` and `\\\\` escaping the previous form needed.

**BUG 55 — Pass D rubric judge 10/10 unparseable** (`scripts/lib/stages/stage4_rubric.py`). The naive `s.find("{") ... s.rfind("}")` JSON extractor swallows the entire reasoning prefix when a thinking model emits `reasoning_content` containing stray `{...}` fragments (pseudo-code, unicode escapes, prose). Fix: replaced with `_extract_last_json_object()`, which makes one forward pass tracking string-literal state and brace depth, records all balanced top-level objects, then walks the candidates **last-first** and accepts the first one that round-trips through `json.loads` AND contains a `"scores"` key. Verified with six synthetic cases: clean, thinking-prefix-with-stray-braces, no-json, fenced, trailing-prose, decoy `{"foo":"bar"}` before the real answer — all six pass.

The current run's Pass D was a silent no-op (every moment fell through to "keeping Pass C score") so the Tier-4 Phase 4.4 blend (`0.6 × pass_c + 0.4 × rubric`) collapsed to unblended Pass C. Pass C's selection itself was sound — the user's worry about "all 1.000" scores was visual noise, not a ranking failure (raw_score has been correctly differentiating since BUG 37).

Verification: `bash -n` clean on stage7_render.sh; `python -c "import ast; ast.parse(...)"` clean on stage4_rubric.py and stage6_vision.py; six-case Pass D parser test passes.

Pages touched: created [[#BUG 53]] / [[#BUG 54]] / [[#BUG 55]] in [[concepts/bugs-and-fixes]] with full symptom/cause/fix and quick-nav rows; updated [[concepts/vision-enrichment]] §Score blending to reflect multiplicative-on-raw semantics with a callout explaining the no-op symptom.

## [2026-05-02] update | Dashboard UX — consolidate camera-pan controls + fix HTML cache

User reported (a) the new "AI editing profiles (per-category)" checkbox shipped earlier today wasn't appearing in the dashboard and (b) there were two redundant camera-pan controls (a dropdown option and a separate checkbox).

**Cause of (a)**: `dashboard/app.py`'s `index()` route used `flask.send_from_directory()` to serve `index.html`, which sets `Cache-Control: max-age=43200` (12 hours) by default. Browsers held the pre-style-profiles HTML for half a day after every UI change, making new controls appear "missing" until a hard refresh.

**Cause of (b)**: legacy redundancy. The framing dropdown set `CLIP_FRAMING=camera_pan` and a separate "Face-tracked camera pan" checkbox set `CLIP_CAMERA_PAN=true`. Stage 6.5 / Stage 7 require *both* (`stage6_vision.sh:48` and `stage7_render.sh:228`) — toggling either alone silently fell back to blur-fill. Two controls, one feature.

**Fix**:
- `dashboard/app.py` — index route now sets `Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, must-revalidate` + `Pragma: no-cache` + `Expires: 0` so HTML always reloads. Static JS/CSS still cache normally.
- `dashboard/templates/index.html` — removed the standalone `chk-camera-pan` checkbox; framing dropdown is now the single source of truth, with a tooltip describing both modes.
- `dashboard/static/modules/pipeline-ui.js` — `collectOriginality()` derives `camera_pan` from `framing === "camera_pan"`. `fetchOriginality()` migrates legacy `framing=blur_fill + camera_pan=true` configs to `framing=camera_pan` so users with that combination land on the working mode.

Backend env-var contract is unchanged — `CLIP_FRAMING` and `CLIP_CAMERA_PAN` are still emitted independently. `_state.py` still keeps `camera_pan` as a config field, `config_io.py` still maps it to env var, the pipeline still gates Stage 6.5 and Stage 7 face-track on both. Only the UI source of truth changed.

Smoke tests: `python -c "import ast; ast.parse(open('dashboard/app.py').read())"` passes; grep confirms zero stale `chk-camera-pan` references.

Pages touched: [[entities/dashboard]] (control table updated, cache-header note added).

## [2026-05-02] update | AI editing profiles — all phases shipped

User: "Implement all phases of the plan and don't forget to update the wiki." Reference plan in conversation history (per-category editing profiles to add life and bypass low-quality-content filters; no voice overlay; single dashboard toggle).

**Architectural shape**: When `CLIP_STYLE_PROFILES=true`, Stage 7's per-clip loop dispatches each moment through `scripts/lib/profile_render.py` instead of the legacy blur-fill render. profile_render resolves the per-category profile, normalizes the edit-plan JSON, synthesizes any missing fields, builds a single `filter_complex` graph (zoom punches + freeze + slow-mo + meme/B-roll/chat overlays + kinetic captions + drawtext hook + amix layer for SFX/music + always-on pitch jitter + container metadata strip + GOP/CRF jitter), and runs FFmpeg. On any failure the bash dispatch falls through to the legacy render so the user still gets a clip. Stage 6 vision was deliberately NOT modified — synthesizer fills missing edit_plan fields from the profile, sidestepping the HTTP 400 cascades hit in BUG 51 when over-stuffing the vision prompt.

**New `scripts/lib/` modules** (11 files, all 3.10-compatible):
- `style_profiles.py` — 10 category templates + per-clip seeded resolution + `fingerprint_params()`
- `edit_plan.py` — Stage-6 edit-plan JSON schema + tolerant `normalize()`
- `profile_render.py` — orchestrator (the only one called by stage 7); embedded `_synthesize_plan()` fills zoom punches + SFX cues from profile when vision didn't emit any
- `zoom_punch.py` — split + scale + overlay enable= filter emitter
- `freeze_frame.py` — split/trim/loop/concat for mid-clip freeze (audio-pad helper too)
- `slow_mo.py` — `probe_source_fps()` + `plan_slow_mo()` with ≥50-fps gate; auto-downgrades to a zoom punch on lower-fps source
- `sfx_inject.py` — manifest reader + `amix` adelay/volume layer builder
- `kinetic_captions.py` — Whisper-SRT → karaoke-tagged ASS, 5 presets, on-disk template loader
- `meme_pick.py` — manifest reader; tag-based picker with generic/ fallback chain
- `broll_pick.py` — same pattern, preferred-subfolder hint
- `chat_overlay.py` — Pillow chat-strip PNG renderer; Phase 5 stub that no-ops gracefully when Pillow or chat data missing

**Caption presets** (`assets/caption_styles/*.ass.tpl`): neon, bouncy, clean, news, soft. Each carries `# active_color` + `# scale_pop` metadata that `kinetic_captions.py` parses; on-disk templates override the in-module fallbacks.

**Asset infrastructure rename**: `scripts/fetch_assets.py` → `scripts/seed_libraries.py` (collided with the pre-existing `scripts/lib/fetch_assets.py` Whisper/Piper model-cache helper). Updated `assets/README.md`, `.gitignore`, and the asset-libraries wiki page to match.

**Pipeline wiring**:
- `scripts/clip-pipeline.sh` — added `CLIP_STYLE_PROFILES` env var (default false), logs state, exports.
- `scripts/stages/stage7_render.sh` — added per-clip dispatch inside the render loop, after SRT setup and before the legacy filter chain. Writes `moment_<T>.json` from `scored_moments.json`, calls profile_render, on success records the clip and `continue`s to the next iteration.

**Dashboard wiring**:
- `dashboard/_state.py::DEFAULT_ORIGINALITY` adds `style_profiles: False`.
- `dashboard/config_io.py` adds `CLIP_STYLE_PROFILES` to env mapping + `style_profiles` to extracted POST keys.
- `dashboard/routes/library_routes.py` (new blueprint) `/api/libraries/scan` runs `seed_libraries.py --scan`.
- `dashboard/routes/__init__.py` registers the new blueprint.
- `dashboard/templates/index.html` adds `chk-style-profiles` checkbox + "Scan Libraries" button in the Originality panel.
- `dashboard/static/modules/pipeline-ui.js` collectOriginality + fetchOriginality include `style_profiles`; new `scanLibraries()` function.
- `dashboard/static/app.js` imports `scanLibraries` + exposes on window for inline `onclick`.

**Smoke tests passed**:
- Python AST 3.10 parse on all 11 lib modules + profile_render.py + seed_libraries.py.
- bash -n on clip-pipeline.sh + stage7_render.sh.
- `from dashboard import config_io; originality_to_env(...)` returns the new `CLIP_STYLE_PROFILES` key.
- Module CLIs: `style_profiles hype --seed 1234` → resolved profile dict; `--fingerprint` → 5-field perturbation dict; `zoom_punch --punches '...'` → valid filter fragment with split/scale/crop/overlay/enable; `meme_pick --category comedy --tag laugh --seed 1` → resolved Twemoji `joy.png` from generic/ fallback; `sfx_inject --cues ...` → valid amix layer with 2 SFX paths from on-disk libraries.
- Plan synthesizer for hype 25 s → 2 evenly-distributed zoom punches + matching impact SFX + peak SFX at midpoint + neon caption preset; for comedy 22 s → 2 zoom punches + scratch SFX + bouncy preset; vision-supplied zoom punches preserved unchanged.
- End-to-end: synthetic 30-s lavfi testsrc → comedy profile render → 3.1 MB H.264 1076×1916 (4 px shake shrinkage matching legacy stage 7) MP4, exit 0. Hype 8 s render → 943 KB MP4, 3 zoom punches + 4 SFX, exit 0.
- Bug found and fixed during smoke test: amix `inputs=N` was counting `len(mix_input_segments)` instead of actual stream count, causing "More input link labels specified for filter 'amix' than it has inputs: 3 > 2" when SFX layer string contained multiple labels — switched to explicit `n_mix` counter. When n_mix==1 we now skip amix entirely and rename src_audio to aout to avoid a pointless one-input mix.

**Open follow-ups** (documented in [[concepts/style-profiles]] §Open follow-ups):
1. Stage 6 prompt extension to emit an actual `edit_plan` JSON (currently the renderer synthesizes one). Skipped to avoid BUG-51-style HTTP 400 regressions.
2. firequalizer EQ tilt — computed in `fingerprint_params` but not yet inserted in the audio chain. Pitch jitter + container fingerprint already cover the bulk.
3. Pillow dependency for chat overlay (Phase 5 fully enabled).

Pages touched: created [[concepts/style-profiles]], updated [[index]], [[concepts/asset-libraries]] (script rename + note).
